# Your Commitment to Climate Action Starts with CORE
CORE makes climate action accessible by providing funding, resources, and expert guidance to Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfeld County home and building owners.
[ How To Get Started ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
[ Make A Donation ](https://www.aspencore.org/make-a-donation)
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
[**Free Energy Concierge**](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
Get expert advice on how to find energy & money savings for property improvement projects.
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/grants-and-funding-programs)
[**Grants & Rebates**](https://www.aspencore.org/grants-and-funding-programs)
Apply for funding to alleviate the financial burden that comes with home & building improvement projects.
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/ways-to-give)
[**Leave A Legacy**](https://www.aspencore.org/ways-to-give)
Whether you donate or start a project, your actions leave a legacy for generations to come.
Empowering You to Make a Difference **Where You Live, Work & Play**
For more than 30 years, CORE has helped Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield County communities take action on climate change.
  

﻿We bridge the gap between aspiration and action, providing energy-efficient property improvement solutions for all. This includes connecting homeowners and building owners with specialized contractors and funding options, and offering comprehensive building and retrofit guidance.
[ About CORE ](https://www.aspencore.org/about)
![Aspen CORE workers sitting on top of a mountain](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/_DSC2402-698w.jpg)
Climate Change Threatens
**Our Environment & Our Future**
Climate change is driven by greenhouse gases that cause severe weather, prolonged droughts, glacial melt, and rising sea levels.
  

**In Pitkin County, buildings alone contribute over 56% of greenhouse gas emissions.**
  

That's why at CORE, our focus is on the built environment. Reducing carbon emissions from this sector is crucial for impactful climate action, and we all must work together if we're going to make a positive impact on the future of our community.
[ About Our Impact ](https://www.aspencore.org/impact)
### Our Approach - Our Impact
By Taking Bold Action Today, We Can Ensure a Better Tomorrow
At CORE, our impact extends beyond just the environment. Our work makes the whole community healthier and more resilient. We improve air and water quality, leading to better public health. We help lower energy costs, benefitting everyone, especially those in affordable housing. Additionally, our focus on sustainability reduces climate risks and lessens the burden on emergency responders. Ultimately, CORE creates a ripple effect of positive change throughout our community.
[ How To Get Started ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
[ Make A Donation ](https://www.aspencore.org/make-a-donation)

Funding Criteria
* * *
#  Understanding Funding Basics  

##  Are you interested in receiving funding from CORE for your building improvement project?  

Read the fine print before submitting your application or reach out to our Energy Concierge Team for more information.
[ Contact An Energy Concierge ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00148--281-29-1920w.JPG)
CORE provides funding for residential, commercial, and multifamily building electrification and energy efficiency projects in Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield Counties.
###  Discover If Your Project Qualifies For CORE’s Grants or Rebates  

#### How much funding is available?
Funding is limited. Residential rebates are available for up to $10,000, while commercial and multifamily projects can qualify for rebates up to $50,000. Grants provide funding up to $200,000. Eligibility and funding amounts vary based on project type, location, and participant qualifications. Applications are accepted on a first-come, first-served basis.
#### What is a multifamily building?
Multifamily buildings are defined as complexes with four or more units in the building. Multifamily projects must be in the common area of the building and/or every unit of the building.﻿
#### Does the program change?
While CORE staff attempt to make changes to funding programs before the beginning of each quarter, any aspect of the grant or rebate programs may be changed at any time and without notice. 
### Key Details for Grants and Rebates
Click through the pages to read project-specific criteria or click the link below to open in a new window.

* * *
Residential Rebates
* * *
#  Save Energy and Money with CORE's Rebates  

##  From planning energy-saving projects to providing funding for home improvements, we have you covered.  

[ Apply for a Rebate ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_rebate_application)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC01358--281-29-c0294170-1920w.JPG)
###  Our region's residential building sector emitted 247,800 MT CO2 in 2020. **That’s equivalent to consuming nearly 28 million gallons of gasoline.** Reducing energy consumption in the built environment can have a significant impact on our work to address climate change.  

###  Residential Building Rebates  

Financing for residential building electrification projects is available to community members living in Pitkin County, Garfield County, and the City of Basalt.﻿
#### Energy Efficiency Projects
**Rebate Amounts**
  * 50% of project cost up to $2,500 for standard participants
  * 50% of project cost up to $5,000 for [Priority Community Participants](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants)﻿


[ Eligible Energy Efficiency Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates#ResEE)
#### Fuel Switching Projects
**Rebate Amounts**
  * 50% of project cost up to $7,500 for standard participants
  * 50% of project cost up to $10,000 for [Priority Community Participants](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants)


[ Eligible Fuel Switching Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates#ResFS)
#### Not sure where to start?
Not a problem; we're here to help![Contact our Energy Concierg](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)[e](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)at any stage of your building project. Find answers to other frequently asked questions about rebates on our [FAQ webpage](https://www.aspencore.org/faq).
#### Is your property in Eagle County?
Properties located in Eagle County but outside of Basalt town limits qualify for [special incentives.](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates) Rebates are available for existing single-family homes or individual units in a multifamily building. 
#### Looking for more funding?
You may be eligible for even more funding! Local community members, from teachers and childcare workers to veterans and government staff, may qualify for savings of up to $10,000 on a single residential project, and up to $50,000 for a commercial or multi-family building project. Check out our [Community Priority Participants](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants) criteria or our [Savings Calculator](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-and-local-funding-programs) to see if you qualify for more incentives.
#### After I complete my project, how long do I have to submit my rebate form?
Your application must be submitted within 90 days of completing a project. Invoices must be dated within 90 days of applying for a rebate.
#### Ready to apply for a residential rebate?
Fill out the residential rebate application and our Energy Concierge team will contact you.
[ Apply for a Rebate ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_rebate_application)
#####  Eligible Energy Efficiency Projects  

### Space Heating
  * Replacing electric baseboard heating with a heat pump


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
### Control Systems
  * Programmable thermostat
  * Outdoor temperature reset
  * Variable speed motor/pump
  * Building management system
  * Recommissioning


### Insulation and Air Sealing
  * Roofs
  * Attics
  * Walls
  * Floors
  * Crawlspaces
  * Pipes
  * Ducts


### Design Assistance and Commissioning
  * Major renovations or new construction
  * Energy modeling
  * Engineering design peer review


Pre-approval is required.
### Induction Range
  

Must be switching from gas range.
  

Rebate limited to $500.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
### Electrical Upgrade
  * Smart panels
  * Upgrades outside of an electrification project


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
### Water Heating
  * Switching from electric resistance to hybrid heat pump water heater
  * Switching from natural gas to electric resistance


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
### EV Charging
  

Aspen Electric customers only.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
##### Eligible Fuel Switching Projects
### Space Heating, Water Heating, Snowmelt, and Ventilation
  

Replacing a fossil fuel system with:
  * A heat pump for space heating, water heating, or snowmelt
  * A heat-recovery or heat pump ventilation system


Design costs and electrical capacity upgrade costs associated with a completed heat pump project will be included in the project cost used to determine the rebate.
[ FAQs ](https://www.aspencore.org/faq)
### New Construction
  * All-electric individual homes without natural gas lines, which use heat pump technology for space and water heating and heat recovery technology for fresh air ventilation


Rebates can be requested once final construction design documents ("100% CD's") are provided. Rebate for Community Priority Participants is $20,000 and $10,000 for others.
  

If the building code prohibits natural gas, then no rebates will be provided.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
### Custom Rebates
  

Custom rebates are considered for projects that do not fall within the other project types but produce significant energy savings.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates)
![CORE energy expert speaking with a local homeowner in Eagle County about building efficiency improvements and rebate opportunities.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/IMG_8827-dcb9c160-1920w.jpg)
### Energy Spotlight:﻿
#### Hilleke Family - Woody Creek
With funding from CORE, the Hilleke family completed their all-electric home construction in Woody Creek. Bonus points - their home has a Home Energy Rating System (HERS) rating of nine!
###  Apply for Residential Rebates  

Click the button below to apply for a Residential Rebate and get funding to make your home more energy efficient. Apply today and let CORE help you save money, reduce emissions, and upgrade your home for a sustainable future.
[ Apply For Rebates! ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_rebate_application)
### Questions? We're here to help.
### Sam Johnston
Energy Concierge, Residential Programs

#  Find Maximum Savings for Your Energy Efficiency Projects.  

##  Cutting your carbon footprint doesn't mean you have to drain your savings. CORE can help you save money while saving energy.  

[ Contact Our Energy Concierge ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)
[ Book An Energy Assessment ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_enrollment)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Stott-s+Mill9-1920w.png)
### CORE provides funding for energy efficiency improvement projects for residential, commercial, and multifamily buildings.   

In addition to receiving funding from CORE for energy-saving projects, you may be eligible for additional funding through [Holy Cross Energy](https://www.holycross.com/rebates/), the [State of Colorado](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/federal-funding-incentives/inflation-reduction-act-tax-credits-incentives), or the [federal Inflation Reduction Act](https://www.rewiringamerica.org/app/ira-calculator).

* * *
Benchmarking
* * *
#  Benchmarking Made Easy  

Track Building Energy Use Effectively and Accurately
CORE helps building owners and municipalities benchmark energy and water use, helping our community save time and money - and meet Colorado building performance standards.
[ Benchmark With CORE ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)
One of the most effective ways to save energy and water in buildings is to benchmark. By tracking a building's energy and water use, we can compare it with similar buildings and past data. Benchmarking also provides insights into performance, energy-saving opportunities, and how to prepare for future upgrades.  

![Aspen mountain landscape with snow-capped peaks, representing the natural environment CORE is working to protect in the Roaring Fork Valley.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/downtown-aspen-buildings-e51c4e1d-23f7f37e-1920w.webp)
###  CORE Can Benchmark For You  

CORE simplifies the benchmarking process for building owners in our community by:
﻿
  * Scheduling site visits to assess the buildings
  * Collecting consent to access utility information* 
  * Recording utility meter information 
  * Collecting building energy and water use data from utility providers
  * Submitting utility data to local and state government program administrators
  * Providing benchmarking reports with utility-use data 
  * Helping select a compliance pathway to meet building performance standard regulations
  * Providing tailored suggestions to reduce building energy use 


  

*Your building’s energy data remains confidential and is shared only with building managers and regulatory agencies.
###  **Meeting Standards, Making Progress**  

The [State of Colorado](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/bpc) requires all commercial, multifamily, and public buildings 50,000 square feet or greater to benchmark. Some local municipalities have additional requirements.
  

CORE partners with local governments to benchmark buildings in these areas:  

  * [City of Aspen – Building IQ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-iq)
  * [Eagle County](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-county-building-performance)
  * Garfield County
  * Town of Basalt 
  * Town of Snowmass Village


  

Benchmarking has been adopted throughout Colorado because benchmarking helps us:
  * Understand a building’s energy and water use
  * Identify energy upgrade opportunities
  * Prepare for electrification and efficiency improvements
  * Reduce operating costs with short- and long-term savings
  * Meet Colorado’s building performance requirements
  * Position buildings as models in sustainability


  

![CORE staff presenting at a community event in Eagle County, highlighting grant opportunities and the impact of local climate initiatives.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00148--281-29-d3c01661-1920w.JPG)
### Questions? I am here to help.
### Julia Wilson
Programs Manager
Email Julia

* * *
Eagle County Rebates
* * *
# Energy Savings for
#  Eagle County Residents  

##  We’re here to help Eagle County residents lower energy use at every stage.  

Whether you're planning energy-efficient upgrades or need assistance with the costs of home improvements, we’ve got the support you need.
[ Apply for a Rebate ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_rebate_application)
![CORE energy expert speaking with a local homeowner in Eagle County about building efficiency improvements and rebate opportunities.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00295--281-29-1920w.JPG)
Eagle County communities are committed to **reducing emissions by 25% by 2025, 50% by 2030, and 80% by 2050** , compared to 2014 levels. Reaching these goals will require the participation of every resident. Ready to make a difference? Get started on your electrification projects today.  

###  Eagle County Residential Building Rebates  

This funding breakdown is for Eagle County residents **who do not live within the town of Basalt**. If your property is within Basalt town limits, [visit our general residential rebates page](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates). Rebates are available for existing single-family homes or individual units in a multifamily building. 
####  Residential Energy Efficiency Projects
  * Rebates amount to 50% of the project cost up to $2,500
  * Residents of Eagle County (outside of the town of Basalt)
  * An energy assessment is required, free of charge


[ Energy Efficiency Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates#EagleCountyResidentialEEProjects)
#### Residential Fuel Switching Projects
  * Rebates amount to 50% of the project cost up to $7,500
  * Residents of Eagle County (outside of the town of Basalt)
  * An energy assessment is required, free of charge﻿


[ Fuel Switching Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates#EagleCountyResidentialFSProjects)
###  Eagle County Commercial and Multifamily Building Rebates  

This funding breakdown is for Eagle County residents **who do not live within the town of Basalt**. If your property is within Basalt town limits, [visit our general commercial and multifamily rebates page](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding). Rebates are available for existing buildings unless otherwise noted. Multifamily buildings are defined as complexes with four or more units in the building. Multifamily projects must be in the common area of the building and/or every unit of the building. 
#### Commercial and Multifamily
#### Energy Efficiency Projects
  * Rebates amount to 50% of the project cost up to $5,000
  * Residents of Eagle County (outside of the town of Basalt)


[ Energy Efficiency Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates#EagleCountyCommercialEEProjects)
#### Commercial and Multifamily
#### Fuel Switching Projects
  * Rebates amount to 50% of the project cost up to $5,000
  * Residents of Eagle County (outside of the town of Basalt)  



[ Fuel Switching Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates#EagleCountyCommercialFSProjects)
#### Not sure where to start?
Not a problem; we're here to help! [Contact our Energy Concierge](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)at any stage of your building project. Find answers to other frequently asked questions about rebates on our [FAQ webpage](https://www.aspencore.org/faq).
#### Is your building 50,000 square feet or larger?
The State’s [Building Performance Colorado](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/bpc) program requires large commercial, multifamily, and public buildings to benchmark utility data and select a building performance compliance pathway. [Eagle County](https://www.eaglecounty.us/departments___services/community_development/index.php) is partnering with CORE to provide free, personalized support for select property owners and managers to meet these targets. Custom rebates may be available for your large commercial or multifamily building.
[ Work with CORE ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-county-building-performance)
#### Looking for more funding?
You may be eligible for even more funding! Local community members, from teachers and childcare workers to veterans and government staff, may qualify for savings of up to $15,000 on a single residential project, and up to $50,000 for a commercial or multi-family building project. Check out our [Community Priority Participants](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants) criteria or our [Savings Calculator](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-and-local-funding-programs) to see if you qualify for more incentives.
#### After I complete my project, how long do I have to submit my rebate form?
Your application must be submitted within 90 days of completing a project. Invoices must be dated within 90 days of applying for a rebate.
#### Ready to apply for a rebate?
Fill out the residential or commercial and multifamily rebate application and our Energy Concierge team will contact you.
[ Residential Rebate Application ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_rebate_application)
[ Commercial and Multifamily Rebate Application ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/business_rebateapp)
#####  **Eligible Energy Efficiency Projects**  

### Space Heating
  * Replacing electric baseboard heating with a heat pump


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
### Control Systems
  * Programmable thermostat
  * Outdoor temperature reset
  * Variable speed motor/pump
  * Building management system
  * Recommissioning


### Insulation and Air Sealing
  * Roofs
  * Attics
  * Walls
  * Floors
  * Crawlspaces
  * Pipes
  * Ducts


### Design Assistance and Commissioning
  * Major renovations or new construction
  * Energy modeling
  * Engineering design peer review


Pre-approval is required.
### Induction Range
Must be switching from gas range.
  

Rebate limited to $500.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
### Electrical Upgrade
  * Smart Panels
  * Upgrades outside of an electrification project


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
### Water Heating
  * Switching from electric resistance to hybrid heat pump water heater
  * Switching from natural gas to electric resistance


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
### EV Charging
Aspen Electric customers only.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
##### Eligible Fuel Switching Projects
### Space Heating, Water Heating, Snowmelt, and Ventilation
  

Replacing a fossil fuel system with:
  * A heat pump for space heating, water heating, or snowmelt
  * A heat-recovery or heat pump ventilation system


Design costs and electrical capacity upgrade costs associated with a completed heat pump project will be included in the project cost used to determine the rebate.
[ FAQs ](https://www.aspencore.org/faq)
### New Construction
  

Rebates can be requested once final construction design documents ("100% CD's") are provided.
  * All-electric individual homes without natural gas lines, which use heat pump technology for space and water heating and heat recovery technology for fresh air ventilation


If the building code prohibits natural gas, then no rebates will be provided.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
### Custom Rebates
  

Custom rebates are considered for projects that do not fall within the other project types but produce significant energy savings.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-rebates)
![Group of volunteers planting trees at a community sustainability event hosted by CORE in the Roaring Fork Valley.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00361--281-29-1920w.JPG)
### Energy Spotlight﻿
#### English in Action - El Jebel
* * *
For nearly 20 years, English In Action has been operating in an aging 1,800-square-foot modular building. On May 1, 2024, thanks to the community's support, including a $40,000 grant from CORE, English In Action broke ground on a new 6,000-square-foot, brick-and-mortar, all-electric English In Action Center for Communications. 
  
They plan to open their doors in 2025 to welcome their growing network of more than 400 learners, 300 volunteers, and 10 staff into a safe, welcoming, energy-efficient community learning and activity center.

About

#  About CORE  

## CORE is a 501(c)(3) nonprofit accelerating the transformation to a sustainable future through action-oriented solutions to the climate crisis. 
CORE turns vision into reality by actively pursuing electrification efforts and addressing the primary sources of greenhouse gas emissions in our valley, preserving the remarkable place we call home. We are able to continue our work with the support of our member organizations, sponsors, and donors.  

**Since 1994** , CORE has used **innovation, connectivity and community** to tackle climate change.
Together, we:  

[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/about)
Removed over **34,000 metric tons of carbon** through 6,000 energy efficiency projects.
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/blog)
Connected community members and businesses with over **$10 million in grants and rebates.**
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/coal-basin-methane-project)
Advanced mitigation efforts to**eliminate massive amounts of methane** leaching from an abandoned coal mine.
### At our CORE, we are guided by our:
#### Purpose
We believe CORE is uniquely positioned to significantly curb carbon emissions in the built environments of Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield County communities and effectively create a region where everyone can live, work, and recreate sustainably.
  

#### Mission
CORE is a 501(c)(3) nonprofit organization urgently reducing carbon emissions through optimizing efficiency, electrification, and resiliency of the built environment, while advancing innovative climate-saving solutions.   

![A group of people is posing for a picture while holding drinks on an outdoor patio.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/_DSC8523--282-29-698w.jpg)
![A group of people is posing for a picture in a dimly lit room. ](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC01916-9c7da119-698w.jpg)
#### Vision
100% of buildings in Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield County communities are electric, efficient, and contributing to the region’s health, safety, and resiliency.
  

#### Impact
A region where individuals, businesses, and government connect ideas, people, and resources to take collective action to slow the pace of climate change.  

#### Values
  

###### Action
We are driven by results.
  

###### Accountability
We deliver on our promises.
  

###### Environmental Justice
Our processes, experience, and solutions are accessible to every community.
  

###### Innovation
We adapt and respond to opportunity.
  

###### Collaboration
We work together with those advancing a shared vision.  

![Randy Udall, a man wearing a winter cap and a red coat, sits in front of a mountain range.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/P1110650-97df363d-34582a20-698w.jpg)
### Setting our sights high
The following are CORE's strategic goals outlined in our Strategic Plan (amended 2025).
  

  * Goal 1: Achieve verifiable and community-focused reductions of carbon emissions.  



  

  * Goal 2: Support under-resourced and workforce communities to reduce carbon emissions.


  

  * Goal 3: Demonstrate organizational excellence in regional climate action knowledge and capacity building in the built environment.


  

  * Goal 4: Seek out and pursue high-impact greenhouse gas reduction demonstration projects with potential for exceeding the return on investment of existing programs and projects.


  

  * Goal 5: Diversify and increase sustainable funding that meets or exceeds the board-approved annual operating budget.

* * *
Federal, State & Local Funding Programs
* * *
#  Find More Financial Incentives to Increase Your Savings  

Stack federal, state, and local incentives for your next project.
Check out the programs below for funding opportunities for your building project. Feeling overwhelmed and not sure where to start? Contact our Energy Concierge team, and we'll help you find the right program for you!
[ Contact An Energy Concierge ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)
According to the [2023 Greenhouse Gas Emissions Report](https://www.aspencore.org/emissions-inventory), **building emissions decreased 1%** despite rising energy consumption. This means we have the opportunity to **make a significant impact** by electrifying and improving energy efficiency in our buildings. Thankfully, there are numerous programs at the federal, state, and county levels to help you make those improvements.  

###  Savings Calculator by Rewiring America  

Explore different savings programs for electrification and energy efficiency projects. See which programs you could be eligible for by entering your information below.
### APCHA's Essential Repairs Program
The Aspen/Pitkin County Housing Authority’s (APCHA) Essential Repairs Program provides up to $10,000 to qualified APCHA homeowners to address critical repairs that enhance the health, safety, and longevity of their homes. Eligible repairs include:
  * Furnace and water heater replacements
  * Roof repairs
  * Plumbing fixes
  * Accessibility modifications
  * Window repairs or replacements
  * Mold remediation


Applications are accepted on a rolling basis until funds are fully allocated. Households with an income of [150% AMI or lower](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants#PitkinAMI) qualify for a [free energy assessment](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-assessments).
[ APCHA's Essential Repair Program ](http://apcha.org/399/Essential-Repair-Program)
![Creating a more sustainable future for Aspen through local climate action.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/CORE+311+Independence+PL.9.1.22.482-1920w.JPG)
![Holy Clean Energy Logo with Aspen CORE](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HCE_Color_2023+%281%29-1920w.png)
### Holy Cross Customers
Holy Cross Energy offers customers a [variety of energy efficiency and electrification upgrades](https://www.holycross.com/member-programs/energy-efficiency-and-rebates). Customers in good standing can receive rebates for:
  * Heating, cooling, and appliances
  * Insulation and air sealing
  * Controls and thermostats
  * Electric transportation and lawn care


If you are a Holy Cross Energy customer, submit your request for rebates to CORE and Holy Cross in a single application for either residential or commercial projects below.
[ Residential Rebate Application ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_rebate_application)
[ Commercial Rebate Application ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/business_rebateapp)
### ReEnergize Eagle County
This program helps full-time Eagle County residents get a free comprehensive energy assessment, energy coaching, and home improvements. Households with an income up to [150% AMI](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants#EagleCountyReEnergize) may receive up to $7,500 for:
  * Insulation, air sealing, duct sealing
  * LED lighting and programmable thermostats
  * Heating/Cooling system, water heater
  * Kitchen stove
  * Refrigerator
  * Spot ventilation


Applicants **MUST** submit one of the following items as income verification: Most recent Tax Return-IRS Form 1040, Wages, or Tax Statement W-2 (please remove Social Security Number from documents).
[ Learn More ](https://hub.walkingmountains.org/reenergize-eagle-county-contact-us)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/ReEnergize-ad67f9a7-1920w.jpg)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/3-1920w.png)
### ReEnergize Garfield County
Residents of Garfield County may receive a free home energy assessment and funding for home energy improvements. Qualifying households are limited to up to [150% AMI](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants#GarfieldAMI). Measures that may be funded, subject to the home energy assessment, include:
  * Insulation & air sealing
  * Pipe & duct wrapping
  * Heating/cooling system upgrade
  * LED lighting


This is a program of [Garfield Clean Energy](https://garfieldcleanenergy.org/reenergize/) and is managed by [CLEER](http://www.cleanenergyeconomy.net/). funding is awarded on a first-come, first-served basis.   

[ Learn More ](https://garfieldcleanenergy.org/reenergize/)
### Colorado HEAR Program
HEAR (Home Electrification and Appliance Rebate) lowers the up-front cost of specific electric upgrades in existing Colorado homes. Rebates are taken as a point-of-sale discount through participating contractors. 
  

Households at or below 150% AMI may receive up to $14,000 for:
  * Heat Pumps
  * Heat Pump Water Heaters
  * Electrical Panel Upgrades
  * Insulation/Air Sealing
  * Electric Stoves


  

Currently available for single-family homes; expanding to condos, apartments, and manufactured homes in 2026. HEAR can be stacked with Colorado tax credits and local utility programs for greater savings.
  

To get started, verify your income through the [Colorado Energy Office portal](http://portal.neighborlysoftware.com/ENERGYREBATES-CO).
[ Learn More ](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/home-energy-rebates)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Colorado-Energy-Office-Logo-1920w.png)

Commercial & Multifamily Funding
* * *
#  Get up to $200,000 to Advance Your Commercial or Multifamily Project  

## Save energy and money without breaking the bank. CORE provides funding for energy efficiency and electrification projects through grants and rebates.
[ Apply for a Commercial or Multifamily Rebate ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/business_rebateapp)
![Aspen CORE connects locals with sustainable solutions and expert energy guidance.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/18-1-1920w.png)
Electrification projects in our commercial and multifamily building sector have the potential to make the biggest impact on reducing greenhouse gas emissions and reaching our climate action goals. Energy efficiency projects can also produce meaningful reductions in greenhouse gas emissions.  

###  Commercial and Multifamily Building Rebates  

Funding for commercial and multifamily building electrification projects is available to community members living in Pitkin County, Garfield County, and Eagle County. Rebates are available for existing buildings unless otherwise noted. Multifamily buildings are defined as complexes with four or more units in the building. Multifamily projects must be in the common area of the building and/or every unit of the building. 
#### Energy Efficiency &   
Fuel Switching Projects
**Rebate Amounts**
  * 50% of the project cost up to $25,000 for standard participants
  * 50% of the project cost up to $50,000 for [Community Priority Participants](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants)


[ View Eligible Projects ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding#1638107047)
#### Grant Eligible
#### ﻿Projects
**Commercial and Multifamily Applicants Only**
  * Grant awards can be up to $200,000
  * Applications accepted on a rolling basis


﻿
  

[ View Grant Info ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding#1489604286)
#### Not sure where to start?
Not a problem; we're here to help! [Contact our Energy Concierge](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) at any stage of your building project. Find answers to other frequently asked questions about rebates on our [FAQ webpage](https://www.aspencore.org/faq).
#### Looking for more funding?
You may be eligible for even more funding! Local community members, from teachers and childcare workers to veterans and government staff, may qualify for savings of up to $10,000 on a single residential project, and up to $50,000 for a commercial or multifamily building project.
  

Check out our [Community Priority Participants](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants) criteria or our [Savings Calculator](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-and-local-funding-programs) to see if you qualify for more incentives.
  

Plus, CORE can help you find and unlock additional funding beyond the rebates we can provide.
#### Ready to apply for a commercial or multifamily rebate?
Fill out the commercial or multifamily rebate application, and our Energy Concierge team will contact you.
[ Apply for a Rebate ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/business_rebateapp)
#####  Eligible Commercial or Multifamily   
Energy Efficiency & Fuel Switching Projects  

### EV Charging
Aspen Electric customers only.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
### Insulation and Air Sealing
  * Roofs
  * Attics
  * Walls
  * Floors
  * Crawlspaces
  * Pipes
  * Ducts


### Appliances and Cooking
  * Heat pump clothes dryers replacing natural gas
  * Commercial induction cooktop/stove replacing natural gas
  * Commercial kitchen projects


[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
### Design Assistance and Commissioning
  * Pre-approval is required
  * Major renovations or new construction
  * Energy modeling
  * Engineering design peer review
  * Commissioning when not required by code


### Control Systems
  * Programmable thermostat
  * Outdoor temperature reset
  * Demand controlled ventilation
  * Variable speed motor/pump
  * Building management system
  * Recommissioning


### Data Management Equipment and Cooling
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
### Space Heating, Water Heating, Snowmelt, and Ventilation
  

Replacing a fossil fuel system with:
  * A heat pump for space heating, water heating, or snowmelt
  * A heat-recovery or heat pump ventilation system


Design costs and electrical capacity upgrade costs associated with a completed heat pump project will be included in the project cost used to determine the rebate.
[ FAQs ](https://www.aspencore.org/faq)
### Custom Rebates
  

Custom rebates will be considered for projects that do not fall within the previous project types but produce significant energy savings.
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
### Energy Spotlight
#### CCY Architects
By awarding a $20,000 grant and advising, CORE’s support enabled CCY Architects to install a heat pump rooftop unit (RTU) project, which heats and cools the office building with 100% electricity and replaced their aging gas RTU.
[ Read More About CCY's Impact ](https://www.ccyarchitects.com/perspective/core-collaboration)
##### Grant Eligible Projects
Grants are intended for larger, long-term, and more impactful projects where rebates are not enough to fulfill the project needs and where grants can make the difference in completing the project.
  

Energy efficiency and building electrification projects in existing buildings are the focus of CORE’s grant program, but applications for new construction are also considered. Grants are awarded for implementation projects only; design work is supported through the [**rebates**](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates).
  

Grant applications are accepted on a rolling basis as funds allow. CORE staff works with interested parties to analyze the greenhouse gas impact of a project before an application is submitted. **Contact our Energy Concierge team to discuss your interest in applying for a grant.**
[ Contact Energy An Concierge ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)
##  Apply for Commercial and Multifamily Rebates  

Click the button below to start your Commercial or Multifamily rebate application and unlock up to $200,000 in funding. Don’t wait—apply today and let CORE help make your energy efficiency or electrification project a reality.
[ Apply For Rebates ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/business_rebateapp)

#  We're driving energy-saving solutions in our community  

## Learn about how we work with community members, business owners, and local government to collectively tackle climate change head-on.
[ Read Our Latest Blogs ](https://www.aspencore.org/blog#Blogs)
![Aspen CORE connects locals with sustainable solutions and expert energy guidance.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/IMG_9531-a054541b-1920w.JPG)
## Energy Spotlight﻿
## Blue Lake Preschool at Stotts Mill
The new all-electric Blue Lake Preschool at Stotts Mill expands childcare access in Basalt while prioritizing sustainability. The advice and funding from CORE ensured a high-efficiency design that benefits both the community and the environment.

## Press Releases
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

Contractor RFQ
* * *
# About CORE's Contractor Directory﻿
CORE assists property owners in Pitkin, Garfield, and Eagle Counties with low to no-cost property assessments to identify efficiency and electrification opportunities. We help owners and residents save energy, reduce costs, and lower greenhouse gas emissions.
  

Our [Contractor Directory](https://www.aspencore.org/contractors) connects qualified local contractors with property owners seeking to implement energy efficiency, electrification, and decarbonization projects.  
  

[ Contractors Apply Here ](https://forms.gle/3TVrNsoXXGzhMGTP8)
**CORE's Service Territory** : Roaring Fork Valley, Garfield County, and Eagle County.
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Aspen+Art+Museum.1.24.23.457-c7b0c536-1920w.JPG)
###  Contractor Requirements  

  * Provide services to clients in CORE's service territory (Roaring Fork Valley, Garfield County, and/or Eagle County)  
  

  * Meet [CORE's Contractor Requirements](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE-s+Contractor+Requirments.pdf)
  * If currently enlisted as a preferred or approved contractor with Holy Cross Energy, Love Electric, Xcel, Collective Clean Energy Fund (CCEF), Colorado Energy Office home energy rebate programs (HEAR/HER), or registered with EPA for Audits, this will satisfy CORE's accreditation requirements.  
  

  * Complete the Request for Information/Qualifications form


  

**Important** : Listing in the Directory is not a guarantee of work. CORE reserves the right to remove companies from the Directory if complaints are received.
### Benefits of Joining CORE's Contractor Directory
**Market Visibility**
Enhanced brand recognition and exposure to property owners actively seeking contractors.
**Project Pipeline**
Access to customers assisted by CORE Project Managers on large retrofit projects.
**Incentive Knowledge**
Understanding of how to leverage CORE incentives for better project feasibility.
**Professional Development**
Access to training, education, and networking opportunities.
### Ready to Join Our Contractor Directory?
###   

Complete the application to get started. The form includes file upload requirements and may take 15-20 minutes to complete.
[ Complete Contractor RFQ Form ](https://forms.gle/3TVrNsoXXGzhMGTP8)
### **Questions? We're here to help.**
### Lee Macke
Project Manager
Email Lee

* * *
Community Priority Participants
* * *
#  Community Priority Participants  

People make our community thrive, and for our people to thrive, they need safe, affordable places to live.
Local community members, from teachers and childcare workers to veterans and government staff, may qualify for savings of up to $10,000 on a single residential project, and up to $50,000 for a commercial or multi-family building project.
[ Review the Criteria ](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants#CPPCriteria)
Deed-restricted housing comprising **70% of Aspen's occupied homes, 16% in Basalt, and 12% in Snowmass Village**. CORE provides these essential residents with resources to save time, energy, and money to maintain safe, healthy, and efficient homes.
### Rooted in Community
We feel fortunate to call the Roaring Fork Valley our home, where awe-inspiring landscapes meet the challenges of rural mountain living.   

  

At CORE, we recognize our community's important role in maintaining this delicate balance. That's why we offer the Community Priority Participant program, designed to support the local individuals and businesses dedicated to the well-being of our neighbors and the environment. 
  

Review the criteria for this program below and elevate your next building project with extra funding – because, in our community, support goes both ways.
### Local Stories
[Read stories](https://www.aspencore.org/blog) about how CORE partnered with community members to drive change through energy-saving projects.   

### Apply For Funding
Apply for [residential rebates](https://www.aspencore.org/residential-rebates) or [commercial and multifamily rebates](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)[.](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-and-multifamily)
  
We also offer [grant funding](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding#1489604286) for special commercial and multifamily building projects. 
  
If you have any questions, our [Energy Concierge](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) team can help you every step of the way.
  

###  Community Priority Participant Criteria  

#### Essential Workers
  * Childcare facility school staff meet qualification criteria by submitting a recent pay stub
  * Local nonprofit and government staff meet qualification criteria by submitting a recent pay stub  
Veterans or active military personnel meet qualification criteria by submitting a photo of their driver’s license or military identification
  * First responder personnel, including volunteers, meet qualification criteria by submitting a recent pay stub or a photo of your ID badge
  * Childcare and school facilities, local nonprofit and government facilities, and first responder facilities qualify on a case-by-case basis; [contact us to inquire](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)


#### Local Workforce
[Aspen Pitkin County Housing Authority](https://www.apcha.org/) (APCHA) and the [Town of Snowmass Village](https://www.tosv.com/143/Housing) affordable housing multifamily buildings qualify for the Community Priority Participant program. 
  * Residents in APCHA meet qualification criteria by submitting a [screenshot](https://drive.google.com/file/d/1AlyI_j17UAIz1cXGQBLwcs89e58uXn1R/view?usp=share_link) of their affordable housing unit management information from the housing authority portal and a piece of mailed address to the same applicant's name(s) and address
  * APCHA Resident Owned (RO) category households must demonstrate an income of 150% of county AMI or lower* 
  * Residents in the Town of Snowmass Village affordable housing program may [contact CORE](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) to inquire. Qualification criteria are still being determined 


  
Other workforce housing residents and multifamily buildings qualify for the Community Priority Participant program on a case-by-case basis; [contact us to inquire](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants):
  * An individual house or condo and with an enforceable commitment to house workforce for employers within the county
  * A multifamily building with an enforceable commitment for 50% or more of units to house workforce for employers within the county


  

*Income must be reported to CORE in a signed statement from the residents’ employer(s). Self-employed individuals must submit the most recent year's tax return.
#### Income Qualified
Individual houses and condos that are occupied by residents with an income of 150% of county AMI (Area Median Income) or lower qualify for the Community Priority Participant program on a case-by-case basis.*
  
Multifamily buildings with 50% or more of the units being occupied by households with an income of 150% of county AMI or lower qualify for the Community Priority Participant program on a case-by-case basis.*  
  
You can find tables for Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield County AMI income levels below.
  

Income-qualified participants meet qualification criteria by submitting tax returns, W2s, or four of their most current pay stubs, with redacted social security numbers.   
  
CORE can also help you navigate additional funding resources that may be available to you. [Contact us for more information.](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
  

*Income must be reported to CORE in a signed statement from the residents’ employer(s). Self-employed individuals must submit the most recent year's tax return.
###### Pitkin County
Pitkin County identifies AMI with the following criteria, as of 2025.
Household Size | 80% AMI | 150% AMI  
---|---|---  
1 | $72,950 | $144,200  
2 | $83,400 | $164,800  
3 | $93,800 | $185,400  
4 | $104,200 | $205,950  
5 | $112,550 | $222,450  
6 | $120,900 | $238,950  
7 | $129,250 | $255,400  
8 | $137,550 | $271,900  
###### Eagle County
ReEnergize is an energy efficiency program in Eagle County that provides critical home energy improvements for income-qualified residents - at no cost! The program is available to households in Eagle County making up to 150% AMI.   

  
Homeowners and renters can receive free home energy assessments, repairs, and funding of up to $7,500 per household to make homes more energy-efficient. Those who heat their home with propane are considered a priority for the program. 
  

Enrollment assistance is available in both English and Spanish. 
  
Contact CORE’s [Energy Concierge Team](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) for more information and help completing and submitting the paperwork. More information is also available on [Eagle County’s website.](https://www.eaglecounty.us/departments___services/resiliency/climate_action/community_programs.php)
Eagle County identifies AMI with the following criteria, as of 2025.
Household Size | 80% AMI | 150% AMI  
---|---|---  
1 | $72,950 | $139,900  
2 | $83,400 | $159,850  
3 | $93,800 | $179,850  
4 | $104,200 | $199,800  
5 | $112,550 | $215,800  
6 | $120,900 | $231,800  
7 | $129,250 | $247,800  
8 | $137,550 | $263,750  
###### Garfield County
ReEnergize is an energy efficiency program in Garfield County that provides funding for home energy improvements for low- and moderate-income households. The program is available to households in Garfield County making up to 150% AMI. 
  
Households with income up to 80% AMI typically receive full funding for recommended improvements, with no cap on the cost. For moderate-income households (80-150% AMI), rebates range from $2,000 to $4,000, depending on income level.
  
Contact [CLEER](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://cleanenergyeconomy.net/&sa=D&source=docs&ust=1737508873601882&usg=AOvVaw1ntY_NUl5ND2ztb1oke-fq) for more information and help completing and submitting the paperwork. More information is also available at [ReEnergize Garfield County](https://garfieldcleanenergy.org/reenergize/)[.](https://www.eaglecounty.us/news_detail_T24_R367.php)
Garfield County identifies AMI with the following criteria, as of 2025.
Household Size | 80% AMI | 150% AMI  
---|---|---  
1 | $59,200 | $111,000  
2 | $67,600 | $126,750  
3 | $76,080 | $142,650  
4 | $84,480 | $158,400  
5 | $91,280 | $171,150  
6 | $98,000 | $183,750  
7 | $104,800 | $196,500  
8 | $111,520 | $209,100  
#### Building Performance Contractors
Contractors that provide services to CORE's clientele, including HVAC, plumbing, and electrical contractors, qualify for the Community Priority Participant program. Contact CORE to inquire about being added to our [contractor list.](https://www.aspencore.org/contractors)
  

If you are a contractor that is registered with the State of Colorado, or you work with an approved contractor who is registered with the State of Colorado, you could be eligible for additional incentives. Find out how to become a registered contractor or who is registered with the [Colorado Energy Office.](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/hptc) ﻿

Business Sponsorships
* * *
###  Become a CORE Business Sponsor  

#### Partner with us and help bridge the gap between aspiration and action.
CORE relies on our partners' philanthropic support to ensure that everyone in our community has access to resources that can help them reduce energy consumption in their home or business.
![Family standing in front of their newly retrofitted home in Garfield County after receiving CORE-funded energy upgrades.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/CCY-Architects_Partners-_3-Olive-and-West-1920w.jpg)
CORE sponsors fuel real impact, advancing carbon reduction, energy efficiency, and community wellbeing across Eagle, Garfield, and Pitkin Counties.  

### Sponsorship Levels
We welcome the opportunity to work with you to create a sponsorship that reflects your business values and goals. CORE offers a range of sponsorship levels, each with benefits designed to increase your visibility and deepen your engagement with our mission.
﻿
At the Sustainability Advocate level and above, additional opportunities, such as event collaborations and co-branded materials, may be tailored to align with your priorities.  

![Family standing in front of their newly retrofitted home in Garfield County after receiving CORE-funded energy upgrades.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC01916-1920w.jpg)
#### Visionary Leader
  * ###### Benefits:
All the benefits of the Climate Champion, plus:
    * 12 VIP tickets to the [Green Expo](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo)
    * Reserved VIP seating at the Green Expo
    * Tailored recognition as a Visionary Leader
    * Special acknowledgment in the CORE e-newsletter
    * Opportunity for name recognition on a CORE educational video
    * Recognition as a Visionary Leader in CORE’s annual Impact Report
    * Recognition as a Visionary Leader on the CORE website
    * Exclusivity in your business sector


#### Climate Champion
  * ###### Benefits:
All the benefits of the Sustainability Advocate, plus:
    * 8 VIP tickets to the [Green Expo](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo)
    * Recognition in Green Expo print advertising
    * Business sponsor testimonial on CORE’s website
    * Recognition as a Climate Champion in CORE’s annual Impact Report
    * Recognition as a Climate Champion on the CORE website


[![Local residents attending a CORE energy efficiency fair in the Roaring Fork Valley, exploring clean energy solutions and speaking with experts.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/240814_core_stirling_039-e29fc9ff-1920w.jpg)](https://www.aspencore.org/)
![Attendees enjoying a CORE-sponsored community sustainability event, surrounded by interactive exhibits and solar-powered demonstrations in Aspen.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/240814_core_stirling_052-e9f5fdb3-1920w.jpg)
### Sustainability Advocate
  * ###### Benefits:
All the benefits of the Efficiency Ally, plus:
    * 6 VIP tickets to the [Green Expo](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo)
    * Recognition in CORE’s e-newsletter
    * Recognition in a print thank you ad
    * Recognition as a member of the Stirling Giving Society
    * Recognition as a Sustainability Advocate in CORE’s annual Impact Report
    * Recognition as a Sustainability Advocate on CORE’s website


### Efficiency Ally
  * ###### Benefits:
Recognition at the [Green Expo](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo), with the following event benefits:
    * Recognition on event display
    * Recognition on event invitation
    * Logo on the registration page
    * Social media mention
    * 4 VIP tickets to the Green Expo
    * A booth at the Green Expo.
As well as these additional benefits: 
    * Recognition as an Efficiency Ally in CORE’s annual Impact Report
    * Recognition as an Efficiency Ally on the CORE website
    * Use of the CORE logo to showcase the partnership and your support of climate solutions

* * *
Building Performance Standards
* * *
#  Turning Insights Into Action  

Choose Sustainable Building Upgrades That Pay Off
The next step after benchmarking is taking action. Building Performance Standards (BPS) require building owners to meet energy performance targets by actively improving their buildings over time. These policies help reduce energy use, lower carbon emissions, and create more efficient, sustainable spaces.
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Aspen+Art+Museum.1.24.23.457-1920w.JPG)
### Higher Building Standards Today for a Sustainable Tomorrow
Buildings account for a significant portion of carbon emissions. Making improvements to our existing building inventory helps achieve decarbonization goals because the majority of commercial and residential building stock that will be standing in 2050 is already built. By implementing energy-saving solutions, we can reduce emissions, maximize investments, address climate change, and ensure long-term sustainability for our communities.  

### CORE Can Help
Once your building is benchmarked, CORE can guide you through the next steps to improve efficiency and meet state and local building performance standards.
﻿
CORE’s services include:
  * Data analysis to help you understand your energy use
  * Compliance pathway selection to meet building performance regulations
  * Tailored recommendations for reducing energy use and emissions
  * Guidance on local and state requirements and strategies for compliance


![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Aspen+Art+Museum.1.24.23.335-1920w.JPG)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/20240822_141900-0a2bb919-1920w.jpg)
### Meeting Standards, Making Progress
The State of Colorado requires all commercial, multifamily, and public buildings 50,000 square feet or greater to select a building performance standards pathway by July 1, 2025. Some local municipalities have additional requirements.
  

CORE partners with local governments to provide building performance support in these areas:
  * [City of Aspen – Building IQ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-iq)
  * [Eagle County](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-county-building-performance)
  * Garfield County
  * Town of Basalt 
  * Town of Snowmass Village


  

Building Performance Standards set energy reduction targets over time, giving owners flexibility to choose the technologies and strategies that work best for them. These policies have been successfully adopted in places like Washington, D.C., New York City, St. Louis, and across Colorado and Washington state.   

### Get Started Today
Making smart building upgrades today ensures lower operating costs, a more comfortable building, and a healthier environment for all. CORE is here to help.  

[ Contact Us to Learn More ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)

* * *
Contractor Directory
* * *
# Find the Right Expert for Your Project
#### Contractors Who Can Bring Your Vision to Reality
Search our contractor directory to connect with local electricians, HVAC professionals, architects, and other tradespeople who can help move your building project forward.
Finding the right contractor can make all the difference in the success of your project. CORE can connect you with professionals who understand energy efficiency, building performance, and our region’s unique needs.
Our searchable contractor directory is a helpful resource for finding local professionals, like HVAC technicians, electricians, architects, and general contractors, who can support your home or commercial building project. You can search by name, company, trade, or location to explore services offered and find contact information.   
  
CORE is not affiliated with these businesses and does not formally vet them. So, we recommend gathering quotes from multiple contractors and checking references when possible.  
  

For the latest recommendations on contractor availability, contact our [Energy Concierge](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) team.   
  

For HVAC projects, please refer to these general categories:
  * **Air-to-Air Heat Pumps** : ducted, split-system, mini-split, and rooftop unit heat pumps
  * **Air-to-Water Heat Pumps** : systems used for in-floor heating, hydronic coils, and snowmelt applications

Please note that contractors may be removed from this list or become ineligible for rebates if CORE receives reports of aggressive sales tactics, dishonesty, project delays, safety violations, or failure to uphold warranties.
