* * *
Eagle County Building Performance
* * *
#  Working Together to Create Better Efficiency  

#### Eagle County Helps Building Owners Meet State Standards
CORE and Eagle County have partnered to help large commercial and multifamily buildings cut carbon emissions and ensure sustainable, comfortable, and efficient spaces for all. By taking action today, we’re preserving Eagle County’s natural beauty and leading the way in environmental stewardship.  

[ Work with CORE ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)
![ECG Logo on the Aspen CORE website](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Copy+of+ECG_Logo_Stacked_CMYK-1920w.png)
Buildings account for nearly 50% of Eagle County’s greenhouse gas emissions, making energy efficiency a key strategy in its climate action plan. To achieve a 50% emissions reduction by 2030, we must improve building performance.
![Eagle County downtown neighborhood on a sunny day.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DylanHBrown_EagleCounty-03112-c4210e5d-0a6655e4-1920w.jpg)
## Improve Your Building Performance  

To support property owners in meeting Colorado’s building performance regulations, Eagle County is stepping up to help. The State’s [Building Performance Colorado](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/bpc) program requires large commercial, multifamily, and public buildings to benchmark utility data and select a building performance compliance pathway by July 1, 2025. These steps will help us meet state goals to reduce large building emissions by 7% by 2026 and 20% by 2030 (compared to 2021 levels).  

## Funding, Resources & Expert Guidance Accessible to You
[Eagle County](https://www.eaglecounty.us/departments___services/community_development/index.php) is partnering with CORE to provide free, personalized support for select property owners and managers to meet these targets. The goal is to help buildings track energy use, improve efficiency, and meet both county and state compliance requirements.
Our [Energy Concierge](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) team can help you: 
  

  * [Get an energy assessment](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
  * Create a step-by-step building design & project plan
  * Navigate building code & policy compliance
  * Access financing options & [stack financial incentives](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
  * Find a [trusted contractor](https://www.aspencore.org/contractors)


  

![two Aspen CORE workers building in a home.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00947-c6f3d868-1920w.JPG)
CORE offers up to $200,000 in funding to advance your building upgrades.  

[ Calculate Savings ](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-and-local-funding-programs)
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00069-d50eb2ac-7bcaca89-1920w.JPG)
## CORE Can Benchmark For You
CORE offers benchmarking services for select Eagle County commercial and multifamily buildings (50,000 square feet and larger) to simplify compliance with [Building Performance Colorado](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/bpc) standards.
  

CORE’s services include:
  * Scheduling site visits to assess the buildings
  * Collecting consent to access utility information* 
  * Recording utility meter information 
  * Collecting building energy and water use data from utility providers
  * Submitting utility data to local and state government program administrators
  * Providing benchmarking reports with utility-use data 
  * Helping select a compliance pathway to meet building performance standard regulations
  * Providing tailored suggestions to reduce energy use 


  

*Your building’s energy data remains confidential and is shared only with building managers and regulatory agencies.
In 2023, buildings in Eagle County **emitted 692.698 MTCO2e.** That’s equivalent to **more than 1,763,000 thousand miles** driven by an average gasoline-powered vehicle.
### Get Started Today
If you are interested in working with CORE to meet Building Performance Colorado requirements, contact our team to learn more.
[ Submit Your Interest to Work with CORE ](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/core_lead)

## Questions? We're Here to Help
### Tim Johns
Associate Project Manager

### Sam Johnston

### Frequently Asked Questions
  * ### I'm looking for funding for my project. Where do I begin?
We recommend starting with our "Savings Finder" here on the website. If you have any questions, contact our Energy Concierge at 1-970-925-9775 x1003. 
  * ### Does CORE still offer grants for residential building projects? 
Grants are reserved for large commercial and multifamily building projects. In 2024, CORE launched a new grants and rebate program designed to focus on projects that have a significant impact on reducing greenhouse gas emissions in the built environment. The new criteria include rebates for residential projects. CORE offers residential rebates for many types of projects. 
  * ### When is the deadline to submit a commercial or multifamily building project grant application?
Grant applications for commercial or multifamily building projects are accepted on a rolling basis. We recommend you contact us before drafting your application so we can help you through the process. Projects must be completed within 18 months of your application being approved. 
  * ### How do I know if I should apply for a rebate, grant, or something else?
CORE only provides grants for commercial and multifamily buildings. So, if you're hoping to do a project in a residential home, you would apply for a rebate. If you are interested in doing a project in a commercial or multifamily building, please reach out to our Energy Concierge team to discuss your options.

# Think Globally, Act Locally
## CORE works collaboratively with local municipalities to cut carbon in the Roaring Fork Valley
Recognizing that we’re stronger together, these valued partners contract with CORE to provide energy saving programs and services.  

Our local governments are turning climate ambition into real-world impact—leading the way with bold policies, smart planning, and community-driven solutions.  

###  City of Aspen  

A black and white drawing of a star on a white background.
Partner since: 1994
A black and white drawing of a group of people in circles.
Population: 7170
A black and white icon of a car with smoke coming out of it.
Emissions Goal: 63% reduction by 2030, net zero by 2050 (below 2017 levels)
The letter i is in a circle on a white background.
Website: [aspen.gov](http://aspen.gov)

# Bill Stirling: A Lifetime of Climate Action
August 20, 2024
Bill Stirling devoted 30 years to CORE, our community, and the environment. He represents altruism, giving back, and making climate action possible for everyone, for a better tomorrow.
  

“My life has really been about trying to make things better in the world and bringing about positive change,” Bill said.
  

Bill Stirling’s journey began in Gainesville, Florida, before taking him to Kenya as a Peace Corps volunteer from 1964-1966. His commitment to service continued as he taught in Harlem and Fort Dix, New Jersey. In 1972, Bill moved to Aspen, Colorado, where he launched Stirling Homes in 1978.
  

As Mayor of Aspen from 1983 to 1991, Bill shaped the city’s future by preserving its charm through restrictions on development, codifying historic preservation, and implementing [Real Estate Transfer Taxes (RETT)](https://www.aspen.gov/1428/Real-Estate-Transfer-Taxes) for affordable housing. His tenure also saw the creation of the [Roaring Fork Transit Authority (RFTA)](https://www.rfta.com/our-mission/), the installation of clean energy projects like the Ruedi Reservoir generator and Maroon Creek hydro project, and the formation of the Aspen Energy Efficiency Committee (AEEC).
  

In 1994, Bill transformed AEEC and Energy 2000 into the Community Office for Resource Efficiency (CORE), with Randy Udall and Lynn Haines as co-directors, to lead regional climate action and greenhouse gas reduction.
  
“I realized it was high time to stop talking about doing something and finally do something,” Bill Stirling said. "We were trying to come to grips with all the things that were going on here with climate change. One of the first warnings for us was that the ski [resort] was losing a few days of winter in the spring and a few days of winter in the fall. We started with the low-hanging fruit, like changing lighting, insulating doors, and installing solar panels.”
  
Today, Bill remains a political activist and full-time realtor, serving on the [CORE board](https://www.aspencore.org/about) for all 30 years and chairing multiple times. He continues to support CORE’s mission and [Pitkin County’s goal](https://pitkincounty.com/1560/Climate-Action) of mitigating and adapting to climate change to preserve natural resources for current and future generations. 
  
“Over the past 30 years, I'm incredibly proud of what this organization has accomplished,” continued Stirlilng. “CORE has remained agile and adaptive, playing a key role in initiatives like bringing wind power to Colorado and partnering with [Aspen Ski Company](https://www.aspensnowmass.com/) to build a generator harnessing methane gas from the [closed coal mine in Somerset](https://www.cpr.org/2021/04/21/methane-from-abandoned-coal-mines-could-be-key-to-fight-climate-change-if-only-it-made-more-money/). This effort provided energy for the Roaring Fork Valley. Now, we're once again tackling methane emissions, this time from an [abandoned mine in Coal Basin](https://www.aspencore.org/coal-basin-methane-project) above Redstone.”
  
In August 2024, CORE established the [Bill Stirling Giving Society](https://www.aspencore.org/donate) to honor Bill’s legacy and give CORE a platform to recognize our most loyal donors. [Join us](https://www.aspencore.org/donate) in continuing the work Bill started.

###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
###  [Building a Zero-Emissions Healing Center in Colorado](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
By Julie Kapala • November 9, 2025
Learn how a nonprofit overcame floodplain and zoning challenges to build a sustainable healing center that sets a new standard for green construction.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

###  [Smuggler Park Couple Take the Path Towards Carbon-Free Living](https://www.aspencore.org/smuggler-park-couple-take-the-path-towards-carbon-free-living)
June 4, 2025
Just beyond the Downtown Core lies Smuggler Park, a fabled Aspen subdivision the HOA says is made up of “real homes for real locals.” Two of those locals, Sam and Desi Barney, are using a CORE grant to drive real change when it comes to how their home uses energy.

###  [Designing Better Buildings: Maximizing Your ROI with Energy-Saving Solutions](https://www.aspencore.org/designing-better-buildings)
By Jami McMannes • May 12, 2025
In Pitkin County, buildings account for over 55% of greenhouse gas emissions. As a property owner, your building design choices significantly impact both your bottom line and our shared environment.
[ ![Panel discussion at a CORE event in Pitkin County, featuring sustainability leaders sharing strategies to reduce carbon emissions from buildings.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC01882-8f27aac6-cfca345c-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/atlantic-aviation-pledges-to-core-a-300-000-climate-action-challenge-grant)
###  [Atlantic Aviation Pledges to CORE a $300,000 Climate Action Challenge Grant](https://www.aspencore.org/atlantic-aviation-pledges-to-core-a-300-000-climate-action-challenge-grant)
By Jami McMannes • April 17, 2025
April 17, 2025

###  [Federal and State Tax Programs Sweeten the Deal on Home Energy Improvements](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-tax-programs-home-energy)
By Jami McMannes • February 25, 2025
Tax Day is April 15, and whether you have already filed or are still pulling receipts together, it’s nice to know what tax breaks could help you save - both dollars and the planet.

###  [Lessons in Layering](https://www.aspencore.org/lessons-in-layering)
January 28, 2025
Living in the Roaring Fork Valley means adapting to an ever-changing mountain climate. Outdoor enthusiasts will tell you that the right combination of base, middle, and outer layers is the secret to staying cozy, safe, and energized in varying conditions.

###  [CORE Offers Enhanced Funding & Services to Make Climate Action Accessible Across Three Counties](https://www.aspencore.org/core-offers-enhanced-funding-services-to-make-climate-action-accessible-across-three-counties)
By Jami McMannes • January 23, 2025
January 23, 2025
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Randy_Udall_Winds_WBoyles20110817_0012-b76273e3-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/randy-udall-a-pioneer-in-climate-action-1951-2013)
###  [Randy Udall: A Pioneer in Climate Action (1951-2013)](https://www.aspencore.org/randy-udall-a-pioneer-in-climate-action-1951-2013)
December 5, 2024
Randy Udall was a visionary leader in the fight against climate change. He was CORE’s first executive director, and his efforts laid the foundation for transformative energy solutions across the Roaring Fork Valley and beyond.

[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/about)
Removed over **34,000 metric tons of carbon** through 6,000 energy efficiency projects.

Connected community members and businesses with over **$10 million in grants and rebates.**

Advanced mitigation efforts to**eliminate massive amounts of methane** leaching from an abandoned coal mine.

Regional Multifamily Energy Retrofit Collaborative
* * *
#  Regional Multifamily Energy Retrofit Collaborative  

##  Helping Eagle, Garfield, and Pitkin County communities upgrade multifamily buildings to be more energy-efficient. ﻿
### Living and operating a building in our unique mountain climate presents challenges.  

**We're here to help!**  

The Regional Mutlifamily Energy Retrofit Collaborative, led by CORE, is working to upgrade multifamily properties across Garfield, Eagle, and Pitkin Counties. 
**Our Goal:**  

To make multifamily properties more energy-efficient.
To develop and connect you with the right funding, expertise, and resources to make it happen.
### Thank you to everyone who filled out our questionnaire!
By completing our questionnaire, you're helping us understand how we can best support energy-efficient building upgrades in multifamily properties in our area. Your feedback will shape future resources, including funding, workforce development, and more.
### About Us
The Region﻿al Multifamily Energy Retrofit Collaborative is a group of local nonprofits and government organizations dedicated to supporting multifamily property owners, operators, and residents like you in Garfield, Eagle, and Pitkin Counties. We’re on a mission to help our communities upgrade multifamily buildings to be more energy-efficient and reduce greenhouse gas emissions.
  
The Collaborative members are:
  * [The Community Office for Resource Efficiency (CORE)](https://www.aspencore.org/savings-finder)
  * [Energy Smart Colorado](https://energysmartcolorado.org/)
  * [Holy Cross Energy](https://www.holycross.com/)
  * [Walking Mountains Science Center](https://www.walkingmountains.org/)


  

And, regional partners include stakeholders in: 
  * [Eagle County](https://www.eaglecounty.us/departments___services/public_health/index.php)
  * [Pitkin County](https://pitkincounty.com/1560/Climate-Action)
  * [Garfield County](https://www.garfield-county.com/environmental-health/)  



### What We Do  

The Regional Multifamily Energy Retrofit Collaborative organizations are working together to make big and bold moves to address climate change. Our focus is to reduce energy consumption in the built environment. 
  
Individually, we offer funding, expertise, connections, and resources for our neighbors to make energy-efficiency improvements to their properties. Contact the organization near you to find out how you can take action now:
  * [Eagle County: Walking Mountains Science Center](https://www.walkingmountains.org/)
  * [Garfield County: CLEER](https://cleanenergyeconomy.net/allies/)
  * [Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield Counties: CORE](https://www.aspencore.org/savings-finder)


  
Collectively, we’re on a mission to scale our impact by reducing energy throughout our largest buildings, such as multifamily housing complexes and neighborhoods. Our primary aim for this initiative is to decrease greenhouse gas emissions, save energy, and improve living conditions in low- to moderate-income housing.
  
In 2023, the Department of Energy awarded us a $100,000 Energizing Rural Communities Prize. During “Phase 1”, we utilized this funding to gain a better understanding of multifamily housing needs in our communities as it relates to greenhouse gas emission reduction and are assessing the feasibility of energy-reducing retrofit projects.
  
Applications for “Phase 2” are due July 2024. The Regional Mutlifamily Energy Retrofit Collaborative is finalizing “Phase 1” of this project and is preparing its application to the Department of Energy for “Phase 2”. In “Phase 2,” we intend to identify buildings for retrofitting, conduct energy audits, secure financing, and implement retrofits like air-source pumps, improved insulation, and more.

Building Energy Resources
* * *
# Building Energy Resources
Welcome to CORE's comprehensive resource center for building energy codes and sustainable building practices. Explore training materials, real-world case studies, and essential tools designed to support our community in creating more energy-efficient buildings across Pitkin, Garfield, and Eagle Counties in Colorado.  

[](https://www.aspencore.org/resources#videotraining)
### Code Training Library
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/resources#videotraining)
[](https://www.aspencore.org/resources#casestudies)
### Case Studies
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/resources#casestudies)
[](https://www.aspencore.org/resources#toolsandguides)
### Tools & Guides
Stark beauty of desolate dunes
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/resources#toolsandguides)
### Code Training Library
[](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QPpWgm-mrHQ&t)
### 2021 IECC Commercial Mechanical and Lighting Training
Learn how to achieve IECC compliance for the 2021 commercial mechanical and lighting building codes in this regionally focused training hosted in Basalt, Colorado.
[ Watch Video ](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QPpWgm-mrHQ&t)
[](https://youtu.be/SOExYWdSQzA?si=R3Sy4gkTxyU3nEdf)
### 2021 IECC Residential and Commercial Thermal Envelope Training
Hope Medina of Shums Coda presents an in-person training on the 2021 IECC Residential and Commercial Thermal Envelope building energy codes.
[ Watch Video ](https://youtu.be/SOExYWdSQzA?si=R3Sy4gkTxyU3nEdf)
[](https://youtu.be/xS6iUt_8ASo?si=qT3205h_NaxNLZYA)
### 2021 IECC Residential and Commercial Overview
Comprehensive overview training session covering the 2021 International Energy Conservation Code for both residential and commercial applications, presented in Glenwood Springs, Colorado.
[ Watch Video ](https://youtu.be/xS6iUt_8ASo?si=qT3205h_NaxNLZYA)
### Case Studies
[](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE_Case+Study_CCY_Final_3.14.25.pdf)
### CCY Architechts
Local architecture firm tackles building efficiency with an all-electric rooftop heat pump. Discover how CCY Architects implemented sustainable solutions to reduce its energy consumption and carbon footprint.
[ Read More ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE_Case+Study_CCY_Final_3.14.25.pdf)
[](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE_Case+Study+Response+%281%29.docx)
### Halle Center for Hope and Healing
Local nonprofit utilizes grants from CORE to help fund its all-electric heat pump system and energy modeling. Learn how strategic funding and planning led to successful energy efficiency improvements.
[ Read More ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE_Case+Study+Response+%281%29.docx)
[](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/One+Riverfront+Case+Study+Avon+Colorado.pdf)
### One Riverfront Townhomes
All-electric HVAC, water heating, snowmelt, pool heating, and appliances — including ranges and fireplaces — powered by high-efficiency chillers and boilers, a first for luxury design.
[ Read More ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/One+Riverfront+Case+Study+Avon+Colorado.pdf)
### Alta Verde Neighborhood
Alta Verde is a net-zero, all-electric apartment community combining critical workforce housing with ambitious sustainability goals, including energy-efficient systems and onsite solar to fully offset energy use.
[ Read More ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/Alta+Verde+Case+Study.pdf)
### Wapiti Commons
A high-performance envelope underpins all subsequent systems, paired with cold-climate heat pumps, energy recovery ventilators, heat pump water heaters, and a 6.5kW per-unit solar array to fully offset energy use.
[ Read More ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/Wapiti+Commons+Case+Study.pdf)
### Horse Mountain Ranch Residence
This home seamlessly integrates stunning design, energy efficiency, and sustainability into one cohesive vision, featuring an all-electric split system heat pump with energy recovery for heating and cooling.
[ Read More ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/Vail+Custom+Single+Family+Home+Case+Study.pdf)
### Tools & Guides
[](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE-Energy-Messaging-Toolkit.pdf)
### Energy Code Messaging Toolkit
A guide for local government staff, building department officials and staff, elected officials, and others who want to proactively communicate about the benefits of adopting and enforcing new energy codes
[ Download Toolkit ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE-Energy-Messaging-Toolkit.pdf)
[](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/Energy+Code+Background+%282%29.pdf)
### Regional Code Collaboration Presentation
December 2025 presentation on our region's recent and planned collaborative building code initiatives. Explore how regional partnerships are advancing energy efficiency standards.
[ View Slide Deck ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/Energy+Code+Background+%282%29.pdf)
### A Regional Roadmap for a New Net Zero
The Net Zero New Construction Roadmap is a joint effort to achieve zero carbon emissions in all new buildings by 2030, while maintaining housing affordability and strengthening the local workforce.
[ Download Roadmap ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/ExecSummary_Lotus_RegionalNetZeroRoadmap_FINAL_111324.pdf)
### CORE Energy Code Impact Study
This report examines the Regional Net Zero Roadmap’s impact on new construction in Colorado’s mountain region. Increased standards lower energy use and emissions, with optional upgrades enabling net zero buildings.
[ Energy Code Cost Analysis ](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/CORE+Energy+Code+Impact+Study_Final_v2.pdf)
### Ready to Get Started?
Whether you're a building professional, local official, or community member interested in energy-efficient building practices, CORE is here to support your journey.
[ How To Get Started ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)
[ Make A Donation ](https://www.aspencore.org/make-a-donation)

Ways to Give

#  Join CORE's Donor Community  

## Make an Impact on Our Community
## Today & Into the Future
When you donate to CORE, you champion community health and resilience. You help us bridge the gap between aspiration and action, empowering everyone to reduce their energy consumption. This leads to cleaner air and water, lower energy costs, and a stronger local economy for generations to come.
[ Donate Today & Multiply Your Impact ](https://www.aspencore.org/donate)
In 2025, every dollar contributed to CORE will be matched by Atlantic Aviation at a rate of $1 for every $2 donated, effectively having 1.5 times the impact.
### Commit to the Challenge & Multiply Your Impact
###### Atlantic Aviation has stepped forward with a transformative $300,000 challenge grant to accelerate our climate action initiatives.  

#### How it Works  

﻿
  * For every $2 you donate, Atlantic Aviation contributes an additional $1
  * Your $100 donation becomes $150 in climate action funding
  * Your $1,000 donation delivers $1,500 in impact
  * CORE is committed to raising a minimum of $600,000 this year to meet the challenge, for a total impact of $900,000


![Aspen CORE connects locals with sustainable solutions and expert energy guidance.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00395-ace3153f-1920w.JPG)
![Aspen CORE connects locals with sustainable solutions and expert energy guidance.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/_DSC1652-1920w.jpg)
#### Your Contribution Will Directly Support  

  

  * Reduction of metric tons of carbon dioxide emissions beyond current targets
  * [**Electrification projects**](https://www.aspencore.org/blogroom?utm_source=bloomerang&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=AAaftereventask) in the built environment
  * [**Assessment, advising, and implementation**](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge?utm_source=bloomerang&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=AAaftereventask) of multifamily and workforce housing decarbonization projects
  * Advancement of decarbonization goals outlined in CORE's [**strategic plan**](https://www.aspencore.org/about?utm_source=bloomerang&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=AAaftereventask) ﻿and annual operating plan


  

###### When you support CORE through this challenge grant, you're not just donating, you're multiplying your impact and joining a community-wide movement to preserve our mountain environment for generations to come.
﻿  

![Aspen CORE connects locals with sustainable solutions and expert energy guidance.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/atlantic-logo-4c-cntr-blue-aa94dba1-1920w.jpg)
### Take Action Today: Ways to Give
#### Make an Individual Donation
We make sure that your contributions toward sustainability stay here in your own backyard, leaving a lasting legacy for generations to come.
  

Donate today to fund immediate climate action, curb the pace of climate change, and protect the beauty and viability of our precious home. You can make a one-time gift, or streamline your giving with a recurring monthly donation.
[ Donate Online Today ](https://www.aspencore.org/donate)
"We need people to to see CORE as one of the pivotal organizations of our time - an organization that has the potential to save the planet."
- Bill Stirling, CORE Founder & Former Mayor of Aspen
[ Button ](https://www.aspencore.org/ways-to-give)
#### Join the Stirling Giving Society
CORE founder and long-time board member, Bill Stirling, devoted 30 years to CORE, our community, and the environment. He represents altruism, giving back, and making climate action possible for everyone, for a better tomorrow.
  

The Stirling Giving Society honors Bill’s legacy and gives CORE a platform to recognize our most loyal donors, allowing us to continue the work Bill started. With a gift of $2,500 or more, you can be a part of this high-level network of donors that provides CORE with the essential support needed to conserve our region’s natural resources, cut carbon emissions to mitigate climate change, and continue the work that Bill started.
  

As a member of the Stirling Giving Society, you will be a part of our CORE community, invited to all events, recognized in our annual appeal, and invited to an exclusive event with other members.
Join the Stirling Giving Society
#### Become a CORE Business Sponsor
As a CORE business sponsor, you will accelerate climate action work in the Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield County communities by supporting our day-to-day initiatives, as well as our community outreach through events and programs.
  

Our business sponsorship opportunities include recognition at CORE events, recognition in the CORE newsletter which reaches more than 5,000 like-minded community members, invitations to exclusive events with community leaders, and more.
  

We would love to meet with you to discuss your business giving goals so that we can ensure you get the most and make the most impact with your sponsorship dollars.
[ Become A Business Sponsor ](https://www.aspencore.org/business-sponsor)

### Celebrating 30 Years of Impact
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/about)
Removed over **34,000 metric tons of carbon** through 6,000 energy efficiency projects.
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/blog)
Connected community members and businesses with over **$10 million in grants and rebates.**
[ ](https://www.aspencore.org/coal-basin-methane-project)
Advanced mitigation efforts to**eliminate massive amounts of methane** leaching from an abandoned coal mine.
CORE has a Platinum Seal of Transparency with Candid. Support our work with trust and confidence by viewing our profile on [Candid](https://www.guidestar.org/profile/84-1280543)[.](https://candid.org/)

# Together, We Can Do More
##  Join us at an event to learn, connect, and make an impact today.  

Whether you're a homeowner, business leader, or climate champion, there's an opportunity for everyone to get involved.
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC01721-4a29791f-1920w.jpg)
##### Upcoming Events
  

4/22/2026 [**My Future My Voice**](https://www.facebook.com/events/101-midland-ave-basalt-co-united-states-colorado-81621/earth-day-celebration/812713387926453/?locale=nn_NO)**,** Basalt Earth Day Celebration  

4/22/2026 [**The Future is Local**](https://www.aspencore.org/) , 2026 Aspen Earth Day Community Event
9/11/2026 [**The Green Expo**](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo) , CORE's Annual Event
  

![Earth Day Events at CORE](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00223+%281%29-1920w.JPG)
#### Celebrate Earth Day with CORE!
###### April 22, 2026
CORE is showing up for Earth Day twice. Find us at [My Future My Voice](https://www.facebook.com/events/101-midland-ave-basalt-co-united-states-colorado-81621/earth-day-celebration/812713387926453/?locale=nn_NO)-Basalt Earth Day Celebration on Tuesday, April 22, from 12:00-6:00 PM at Basalt River Park, then head up valley to [The Future is Local:](https://aspennature.org/activity/2026-aspen-earth-day-community-event/) 2026 Aspen Earth Day Community Event, starting with the Community Action Fair, 3-5 pm, followed by a lecture from 6-7:30 pm at the Wheeler Opera House in Aspen.
* * *
#### The Green Expo, CORE's Annual Event
###### September 11, 2026
The 2026 The Green Expo will take place at Aspen Meadows, featuring sustainable businesses, products, and services from across the Roaring Fork Valley and beyond. This free, half-day event brings together industry professionals and community members to explore practical solutions to reduce greenhouse gas emissions.
  

**Sign up for our newsletter to get updates about the 2026 Green Expo and other upcoming events and programs.**  

[ E-Newsletter Sign Up ](https://www.aspencore.org/newsletter#scroll_to_bottom)

* * *
#### Community Partnership Events
We collaborate with local organizations to multiply our impact and create stronger climate solutions. Join us at these partner-hosted events to learn about regional initiatives and connect with fellow change-makers.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/20250605_195644-1920w.jpg)
### Past Events
* * *
###### Aspen Saturday Farmer's Market
September 20, from 8:30 a.m. - 2 p.m. at Galena & Hopkins Avenue, Aspen, CO
  

Since 1998, the Aspen Farmer's Market has been a local's tradition. Stroll through the streets of Aspen to browse Colorado-grown produce, Colorado-produced artisan products, and CORE services! We look forward to chatting with you at our booth. This event is free and open to the public.
* * *
###### Snowmass Concert Series
July 31, 2025, from 5:30 p.m. - 8 p.m. at Fanny Hill, Snowmass Village, CO
  

Stop by our table while you enjoy this long-standing summer tradition and local favorite. The Snowmass Summer Concert Series is a fantastic way to enjoy music with friends (and learn about CORE) in a relaxed atmosphere with a spectacular mountain backdrop. The band on this night will be Goldie Boutilier, a Canadian singer-songwriter known for her cinematic alt-pop sound. This event is free and open to the public.
* * *
###### The Green Expo
September 12, 2025
Presented by CORE, the Green Expo spotlights sustainable businesses, products, and services from the Roaring Fork Valley and beyond. This free half-day event brings together industry professionals and community members to explore innovative solutions that significantly reduce carbon emissions.  

* * *
###### State of the Climate 2024
December 12, 2024 | Hooch Craft Cocktail Bar
  

At CORE's 2024 State of the Climate, we celebrated the legacy of Randy Udall, CORE’s first executive director. Bill Ritter, former governor of Colorado and advocate of clean energy policy, served as the keynote speaker alongside Mark Udall, former U.S. senator from Colorado, and Randy's daughter, Tarn Udall. The incredible turnout and energy made the evening truly unforgettable.
Thank you to all who attended the event. We hope you feel inspired to [take climate action](https://www.aspencore.org/donate) and be part of the solution to climate change.
  

[Read more](https://www.aspencore.org/randy-udall-a-pioneer-in-climate-action-1951-2013?utm_source=Bloomerang&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=Dec-english-newsletter) about Randy Udall’s influence on today’s clean energy initiatives.  

* * *
###### 30 Years of Impact Celebration at Buttermilk
August 14, 2024 | The Backyard at Buttermilk
  

Thank you to everyone who attended our 30-year anniversary kick-off. We honored founding board member, Bill Stirling, for his ongoing dedication to climate action in our community and established the [Stirling Giving Society](https://www.aspencore.org/ways-to-give#StirlingSociety). This esteemed network of donors provides CORE with the essential support needed to reduce carbon emissions to mitigate climate change and carry forward the work that Bill started.
  

We truly enjoyed connecting with those who have supported CORE over the past three decades and are eager to continue working together to preserve our environment now and into the future. Learn more about [CORE's 30-year journey](https://www.aspencore.org/impact) in leading climate action in our community.
* * *
###### The Future of Sustainability Codes
May 30, 2024 | Rocky Mountain Institute in Basalt
  

The Future of Sustainability Codes brought together Roaring Fork building officials, construction industry leaders, and elected officials for a panel discussion hosted by [AIA Colorado](https://aiacolorado.org/). The conversation explored the current state of sustainable building codes and future goals for advancing sustainability in the built environment.
* * *
###### PowerUp: Energize Your Savings
May 23, 2024 | Basalt Regional Library
  

PowerUp Your Energy Savings brought together [USGBC](https://www.usgbc.org/), [Full Circle](https://fullcircleconstruction.services/), [Holy Cross Energy,](https://www.holycross.com/) and CORE for a community discussion on funding energy-efficient building projects. With support from local, state, and federal governments for sustainable building improvements, the event explored available funding opportunities and how to navigate them. Participants gained insights from industry experts on leveraging financial resources to advance energy savings and climate action.
* * *
###### Coal Basin Methane Capture Project
[Coal Basin](https://www.aspencore.org/coal-basin-methane-project) community events were hosted in Basalt and Redstone in 2024. The feedback collected from our outreach efforts helped us frame our application to the [US Forest Service](https://www.fs.usda.gov/project/?project=64062) to request approval to move forward with mitigation efforts.

# Building a Zero-Emissions Healing Center in Colorado
November 9, 2025
# CORE Energy Spotlight:
# ﻿Halle Center for Hope and Healing
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Response_SolarRoof-1920w.png)
  

For decades, the nonprofit [Response](https://responsehelps.org/) has worked to end domestic and sexual abuse in Colorado's Roaring Fork Valley. Its staff operated from a cramped, rented office, and survivors of abuse had no secure, long-term shelter to rely on. The lack of stable housing is a critical gap, as a safe environment is essential for healing and rebuilding lives. This inspired Response to pursue a difficult but necessary dream: building a combined office and healing center. And they added another ambitious goal—the facility had to be a zero-emissions building.
  

This post explores the journey of creating the [Halle Center for Hope and Healing](https://responsehelps.org/campaign/). It’s a story of overcoming significant obstacles to build a sustainable healing center that serves both its clients and the planet. From navigating land use challenges to securing funding, Response's path offers powerful lessons for any organization committed to making a lasting, positive impact.
  

## Challenges and Creative Solutions
When Response found an affordable parcel of land in [Basalt](https://www.basalt.net/), it came with a host of challenges. The property was on a 100-year floodplain, which eliminated the possibility of a basement for mechanical systems. It also had a unique triangular shape and was part of a commercial HOA with strict building height restrictions. These hurdles required innovative thinking and a dedicated team.
  

### Designing for Sustainability in a Floodplain
The floodplain location was a major constraint. To mitigate flood risk, 50% of the building had to be constructed on piers, raising it above ground level. This meant the space typically used for mechanical rooms and venting in a basement was lost. The design team had to get creative, finding space for these essential systems within the main structure without compromising the living areas.
  

### Balancing Privacy and Solar Gain
For a healing center serving survivors of abuse, privacy and security are paramount. However, a key element of sustainable design is passive solar gain, which requires orienting a building to maximize sun exposure. Erica Golden, principal of site-architects, explained the dilemma: "We fought hard for an increase in height...maintaining both security and effective sustainable design strategies." The final design cleverly balanced these competing needs, creating a space that feels both secure and connected to the natural environment.
  

### Navigating Land Use and HOA Relations
The land wasn't originally zoned for a shelter, requiring Response to petition the Town of Basalt for a land use change. Success depended on community support. Response built strong relationships with neighboring businesses and HOA members, authentically communicating their vision and addressing concerns. Their efforts paid off when the HOA agreed to a height variance and the town approved the land use change, proving that partnership and transparent communication are key to overcoming regulatory hurdles.
  

### Securing Funding for an Ambitious Vision
Building a state-of-the-art, $9.75 million facility required a massive fundraising effort. Response secured a diverse mix of funding, including a $4 million grant from the Colorado Division of Housing and significant contributions from local governments and foundations.
  

Grants from the [Community Office for Resource Efficiency (CORE)](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding) were crucial, helping fund the all-electric heat pump system and energy modeling. This multi-faceted approach demonstrates the power of pursuing every available funding opportunity.
  

## Key Features of a Sustainable Healing Center
The Halle Center for Hope and Healing integrates numerous green construction features to achieve its zero-emissions goal. These elements not only reduce the building's environmental impact but also create a healthier, more comfortable space for residents.
  * **Solar Photovoltaic Panels:** The building features a 51.41 kWh solar panel system on its uniquely designed butterfly-sloped roof. This system produces about 70% of the building's energy needs on-site.
  * **Passive Solar Design:** The building’s orientation and window placement are optimized to capture natural light and heat, reducing the need for artificial lighting and heating during the day.
  * **All-Electric Systems:** The center operates entirely on electricity, eliminating the use of fossil fuels. This includes a Mitsubishi multi-zone heat pump system for highly efficient heating and cooling, electric induction cooktops in the communal kitchen, and electric baseboard heaters.
  * **EV Charging Stations:** To support sustainable transportation, the facility includes four Level 2 EV charging stations, supported by a grant from Charge Ahead Colorado.
  * **ADA Accessibility:** The design goes beyond basic requirements to ensure the entire facility, including its two ADA-compliant residential units, is fully accessible and welcoming to all individuals.


  

## The Power of Community and Collaboration
The success of the Halle Center was a true team effort. From the beginning, Response, site-architects, [G.F. Woods Construction](https://www.gfwoods.com/), and other partners shared a unified vision. Eric Wynne, project manager for G.F. Woods, noted the project's success was due to a "cohesive team and well-thought-out design." This collaborative spirit allowed the team to solve problems proactively and efficiently.
  

CORE played a vital role beyond just providing grants. Their staff offered technical advice on energy systems, connected the team with other resources like Holy Cross Energy, and provided guidance on strengthening grant applications. "Having the staff as a resource was just as important as the impact of the funding," said Shannon Meyer, Executive Director of Response.
  

## A Model for a Sustainable Future
The Halle Center for Hope and Healing stands as a powerful testament to what is possible when a nonprofit commits to a bold vision. It is more than just a building; it is a safe harbor for survivors and a model for sustainable, resilient community projects. The center not only provides shelter but also generates most of its own clean energy, with the remainder purchased from [Holy Cross Energy](https://www.holycross.com/)’s renewable sources.
  

"I love that we are a demonstration project for other nonprofits to see you can build in a somewhat affordable manner and meet sustainability goals and not have to be a drain on the energy system," Meyer stated.
  

The project proves that financial constraints do not have to compromise environmental ethics. By prioritizing long-term savings and leveraging grants and tax credits, Response built a facility that is both economically and environmentally sound. This zero-emissions building shows that even on a challenging site, a strong vision can lead to a healthy, healing solution that benefits everyone.
  

## Learn More and Get Involved
The Halle Center for Hope and Healing is a shining example of how innovative construction can support a nonprofit's mission. It demonstrates that with perseverance, teamwork, and community support, even the most ambitious dreams can become a reality.
  

  * To learn more about Response's mission and their work to support survivors, visit the [Response website](https://responsehelps.org/).
  * To discover how CORE supports commercial projects with grants and expert guidance, [explore our programs](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding).

###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

Brittany LaClair

### Brittany LaClair
Associate Director of Development  

* * *
Brittany studied Environmental Studies at the University of Vermont, where she discovered her passion for sustainability, conservation, and energy efficiency. During college, her love of travel took her to Costa Rica and Spain, where she gained an international perspective on environmental issues.
  

After graduation, she set out to find bigger mountains and explore the West, landing in Aspen to work as a snowboard instructor for what she thought would be just one winter. The outdoorsy, adventurous lifestyle quickly drew her in, and she continues to enjoy life in the Roaring Fork Valley.
  

Some of her favorite activities include snowboarding, hiking, trail running, camping, and paddleboarding. Brittany has worked for nonprofits since 2016 and strives to make a positive impact on the community through her work with CORE.

* * *
Cedric Gamble
* * *
### Cedric Gamble
Director of Climate Action Programs  

* * *
Cedric brings a deep love of nature, adventure, and community to the CORE team. Growing up at a YMCA summer camp in the Adirondacks with parents who took the whole family on backpacking and canoeing trips fueled these passions from a young age. After earning an Environmental Science degree from Allegheny College in Pennsylvania, Cedric promptly moved West to pursue a career in the outdoor industry. For 8 years Cedric worked variously as a ski patroller at Park City Mountain Resort, skiing and climbing mountain guide on Mt Rainier, in the North Cascades, Ouray, and Wasatch Mountains. Following the motivation to work more directly on renewable energy and climate change solutions, Cedric transitioned to working in the solar industry in 2018. While working as design engineer and project manager designing utility scale solar energy projects, Cedric completed a Master of Engineering degree from the University of Wisconsin-Madison in Sustainable Systems Engineering. After earning this degree, Cedric pursued an opportunity in Salt Lake City providing energy modeling and energy efficiency advising for commercial buildings in Utah.
  
Cedric is thrilled to work with the CORE team to improve the efficiency of and reduce the greenhouse gas emissions from the built environment in the greater Roaring Fork area. In his role with CORE, Cedric is eager to apply his experience to empower the Program Team in the successful completion of projects and development of energy efficiency and rebate programs. He is motivated by building systems that improve health and drive climate change solutions for all members of the community. Cedric, his wife, 14 month old son, and two dogs are new to the Roaring Fork and excited to explore and put down roots in this special mountain community.  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
[970-233-2230](https://www.aspencore.org/)
A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
Cedric@AspenCORE.org

# Combating Climate Change through Sustainable Farming
July 30, 2024
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/IMG_5399-1920w.jpeg)
On twenty-two acres of land leased from [Pitkin County](https://pitkincounty.com/) and right off Highway 82 is [Two Roots Farm](https://www.tworootsfarm.com/), a beautiful and bountiful farm that provides produce for a 250-member Community Supported Agriculture (CSA), an onsite farm stand, and local restaurants in our community. Owner Harper Kaufam knows the importance of local, organic farming and started the farm in 2016. Her mission is to combat climate change through sustainable farming practices and grow the healthiest food possible while fostering a positive work environment, vibrant soil, and community connection.
  
Harper needed to install a new greenhouse for plant propagation to get her through the winter months. Greenhouses typically rely on a propane heating system, but with climate in mind, she wanted to stay away from fossil fuels. She learned about an innovative way to heat a greenhouse from the [Central Rocky Mountain Permaculture Institute](https://crmpi.org/). It’s called a climate battery and uses the ground temperatures to control the greenhouse temperature. This innovative system will heat in the winter and cool in the summer and will reduce Two Roots’ reliance on fossil fuels, reduce costs, and extend their growing season.
  
CORE is a supporter of new, innovative ideas that lower carbon emissions and help our community thrive, so we provided a $30,000 [grant](https://www.aspencore.org/savings-finder) to fund this project. This project will start in 2024, so stay tuned for an update once the climate battery is installed.
  
Harper is always looking for ways to lower the farm’s carbon footprint whether it's electrifying to use the on-site solar panels or installing a new climate battery. She takes a holistic approach, considering soil health, greenhouse gas emissions, and food quality. Everything is hand-powered instead of relying on diesel machinery, and the plants help sequester carbon. She uses a regenerative process to keep the soil healthy and grows a variety of vegetables such as broccoli, carrots, spinach, and radishes.
  
CORE supports projects that matter to our community and the locals living here. We remove the financial barrier and help more people to take action, bringing equity and inclusivity to the climate crisis. 
  
Give our [Energy Concierge](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge)a call today to learn how you can lower your carbon footprint.
  

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/IMG_5394-af202122-1920w.jpeg)

July 30, 2024
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Coerdert+Case+Study+%281%29-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
###  [Building a Zero-Emissions Healing Center in Colorado](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
By Julie Kapala • November 9, 2025
Learn how a nonprofit overcame floodplain and zoning challenges to build a sustainable healing center that sets a new standard for green construction.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

Deborah Breen
* * *
![Deborah is a blonde-haired woman wearing a black shirt.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Deb+Headshot-1920w.png)
### Deborah Breen
Director of Marketing and Communications
* * *
Deborah oversees CORE’s marketing and communications efforts, bringing more than 20 years of leadership experience in the nonprofit sector to help strengthen CORE’s fundraising efforts and deepen community connections.
  

Her background includes serving as the inaugural President and CEO of the Aspen Valley Hospital Foundation, Chief Development Officer of Northern Dutchess Hospital Foundation in New York, and Director of Development at Vassar Brothers Medical Center Foundation. In each of these roles, she led successful capital campaigns, built strong stakeholder relationships, and developed strategic initiatives to support long-term sustainability.
  

Deborah has also held numerous leadership positions on nonprofit and chamber of commerce boards and served as president of her Rotary Clubs in both Aspen and Rhinebeck. When not in Aspen, Deborah resides in North Carolina’s Outer Banks with her husband, a retired New York State Police Sergeant, and their two dogs. She’s the proud mom of two daughters, one a producer with ABC in Savannah, Georgia, and the other an actress based in Burbank, California.  
  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
1-970-925-9775   

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
Deborah@AspenCORE.org

December 2025 Newsletter
* * *
###  **This December: Celebrating Milestones & New Beginnings**  

What a year it has been! As we wrap up 2025, I'm inspired by the progress we've made together. This year, CORE invested $1.8 million in grants and rebates that helped local residents, businesses, and essential workers cut emissions and build climate resilience. From heat pumps in family homes to energy upgrades at workforce housing, every dollar created real, measurable change. December marks both an ending and a beginning, a time to celebrate achievements while preparing for the exciting work ahead. Here's to finishing strong and stepping boldly into 2026.
  

With Gratitude,
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed-1920w.png)](https://www.aspencore.org/tara-stitzlein)
### Welcome to the Team: Cedric Gamble
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed-1920w.jpg)
We're excited to introduce Cedric Gamble, CORE's new Director of Climate Action Programs! Cedric brings expertise in renewable energy, commercial building efficiency, and sustainable systems engineering, including a master's degree from the University of Wisconsin-Madison. His background spans solar design, energy modeling, and project management. Cedric is passionate about building systems that improve health and drive climate solutions for all community members. 
[ Meet Cedric Gamble ](https://www.aspencore.org/cedric-gamble)
### Energy Spotlight: Obermeyer Place
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%281%29-1920w.jpg)
CORE's grants are delivering real results at Obermeyer Place. This project exemplifies CORE's commitment to reducing carbon emissions in key community projects, including workforce housing.
  

"Getting a CORE grant for our building automation upgrade was a straightforward process with simple paperwork. This helped our HOA, which includes deed-restricted housing, have a system running as efficiently as it can. Our utility costs are trending under budget and the system's online dashboard lets us quickly make adjustments."
  

-Ben Wolff, General Manager, Frias Properties of Aspen Snowmass
[ Explore Commercial Rebates ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
# CORE Projects Making Local Headlines
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%282%29-1815112b-1920w.png)](https://www.coloradogives.org/donate/Community-Office-For-Resource-Efficiency?blm_aid=0)
CORE's community partnerships are generating buzz in local news. Recent coverage highlights our Building IQ benchmarking partnership with the City of Aspen, a crucial first step toward reducing building emissions, and our grant support for Carbondale's new Aquatic Center, set to be one of Colorado's most sustainable municipal pools.

Blog Layout
* * *
# Designing Better Buildings: Maximizing Your ROI with Energy-Saving Solutions
May 12, 2025
## Maximizing Your ROI with Energy-Saving Solutions  

In Pitkin County, buildings account for over 55% of greenhouse gas emissions. As a property owner, your building design choices significantly impact both your bottom line and our shared environment. By partnering with the right architect and the Community Office for Resource Efficiency (CORE), you’ll create a powerful team that can transform your vision into a high-performance reality.
  

**The Building Performance Formula**
  

The most successful projects happen when owners, architects, and sustainability experts collaborate from day one. Look for a design team that aligns with your values and prioritizes sustainability alongside aesthetics and functionality. 
Firms like [CCY Architects](https://www.ccyarchitects.com/) in Basalt demonstrate this balance, designing spaces that "connect people to the natural environment and build community with an evocative design reflective of contemporary life."
CORE completes this partnership by [providing expertise](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) through each stage of construction, including helping you:
  

  * Navigate increasingly stringent building codes 
  * Create customized design and project plans
  * [Connect with experienced contractors](https://www.aspencore.org/contractors) and energy modeling specialists
  * Identify and [stack financial incentives](https://www.aspencore.org/calculate-savings) and financing options from multiple sources


  

**Start with Design Fundamentals**
  

A sustainability-focused architect will recommend strategies that deliver the highest return on investment before discussing expensive mechanical systems. Key foundational elements include:
  

  * **Building orientation:** A properly positioned building can save 10-20% on heating and cooling energy usage, with some achieving up to 40% savings with no added construction costs.
  * **Building envelope:** Well-designed insulation and air sealing deliver significant long-term energy savings with minimal upfront investment.
  * **Strategic fenestration:** The thoughtful placement of windows, doors, skylights, and other openings creates natural ventilation and lighting while enhancing comfort.


  

**Beyond the Basics**
  

Once fundamental design choices are in place, examine how technology investments can further enhance the performance and overall value of your building.
  

  * **Smart building controls** optimize energy use based on occupancy and conditions.
  * **On-site renewable energy** with battery storage offers independence and resilience from the communal energy grid.
  * **Emerging and traditional approaches** , like heat pumps, geothermal systems, and earth-based building materials, combine innovation with proven solutions. 


**  
The Design Difference**
  

The most successful sustainable projects start with a clear vision and the right team. CORE can help you host a kick-off meeting with your architect to align expectations early. We define measurable energy goals, explore design options through energy modeling, and provide quality control during construction.
﻿
Thoughtful architectural design creates value beyond energy savings through increased property value, improved comfort, and lower operational costs. Look for architects who balance today's needs with tomorrow's possibilities in your building project.
  

**CORE is your building performance hub, working hand-in-hand with you and your design team to ensure your projects prioritize environmental responsibility without compromising livability and affordability.**
  

[**Contact our Energy Concierge**](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-concierge) **today to begin building a more sustainable future.**
![CORE staff member conducting a home energy assessment in Aspen, demonstrating their hands-on approach to climate solutions.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/_DWP7870-HDR-1920w.jpg)
CCY Architects transformed its Basalt office into a “living lab” to test sustainable design practices that could later be recommended to clients. This included installing an all-electric rooftop heat pump with CORE’s support. In the first month, gas use dropped from 52 therms to nearly zero, the equivalent of removing 700 miles of an average car’s driving emissions.
* * *
This content is proudly included in the [Randy Udall Memorial Educational Program](https://www.aspencore.org/events), advancing energy education and climate action.
[ < Older Post ](https://www.aspencore.org/atlantic-aviation-pledges-to-core-a-300-000-climate-action-challenge-grant) [ Newer Post > ](https://www.aspencore.org/smuggler-park-couple-take-the-path-towards-carbon-free-living)
Jami McMannes • May 12, 2025
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Coerdert+Case+Study+%281%29-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
###  [Building a Zero-Emissions Healing Center in Colorado](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
By Julie Kapala • November 9, 2025
Learn how a nonprofit overcame floodplain and zoning challenges to build a sustainable healing center that sets a new standard for green construction.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

Emissions Inventory
* * *
#  Pitkin County Greenhouse Gas Emissions Inventory  

## Navigate the report using the tabs at the bottom of the dashboard. 
The Emissions Calculators is a tool that displays the results of the 2023 Greenhouse Gas (GHG) Emissions Inventory Report developed for [Pitkin County](https://pitkincounty.com/192/Building) and the Community Office for Resource Efficiency (CORE).  

This inventory estimated GHG emissions produced in 2023 by the following communities: City of Aspen, Town of Basalt, Town of Snowmass Village, and Unincorporated Pitkin County. The dashboard includes previous GHG inventory data from 2014, 2017, 2019 and 2020.
