# Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer
September 22, 2025
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg)
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer.
  

Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states.
  

“I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” 
  

Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. 
  

She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver.
  

She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative.
﻿
“We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.”
  

And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June.
“This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states.
  

Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at [aspencore.org/green-expo](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo).
  

CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action.
  

For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the [aspencore.org](http://www.aspencore.org/) or contact the organization directly.

What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.

# Leslie Kaplan completes her 100% electric dream home in Basalt
September 30, 2024
### Energy Spotlight: Leslie Kaplan, Basalt  

Leslie Kaplan’s dream of building a fully electric home in Basalt has finally come to fruition, marking a significant milestone in her journey toward sustainable living. She chose to construct a duplex in Stott’s Mill for her family and as a long-term investment.
  
While raising her children in a home with a gas stove, she grew concerned about its potential health risks. Gas stoves release pollutants like nitrogen dioxide and carbon monoxide, which can affect our lungs and make breathing problems worse, and contribute to climate change (“[The Science behind Gas Stoves](https://rmi.org/the-science-behind-gas-stoves/)”, Rocky Mountain Institute, June 15, 2023). With a clean slate, she committed to creating a healthier, sustainable home, and decided to explore her options.
Wanting to learn more about induction stoves, Leslie attended CORE’s Climate Conscious Kitchen event in 2023, where she met Mary Wiener, a CORE Energy Concierge, who guided her toward full electrification. Now, her home runs on heat pump technology for heating and hot water, solar panels for energy, and is completely gas-free.
  
Finding the time, money, and support to make building an all-electric home can feel like an uphill battle but Leslie was able to lean on CORE’s Energy Concierge team throughout the project for guidance. “Leslie was open to new ideas, dedicated to researching her options, and chose high quality appliances,” says Mary. From deciding on electric heat pumps to solar panels and battery storage, Leslie felt supported as she navigated through all the decisions that went into making her dream home a reality.
  
In addition to CORE’s project planning recommendations, Leslie also tapped into CORE’s financial resources. CORE provides funding for energy efficiency improvements for residential, commercial, and multifamily buildings in the form of [Grants and Rebates](https://www.aspencore.org/savings-finder). In 2023, Leslie applied for a CORE grant and was awarded $25,000. She said, “With building an all-electric home with the heat pumps and a few other additions, there was an additional cost incurred… and that [grant] really helped make the improvements to go all-electric a lot easier to afford.” 
  
Now that her project is complete, Leslie is motivated to spread the word and encourage community members to go all-electric. She is eager for others to make the shift to sustainable living and start taking climate action. “My wish for future builders and people making renovations is that they take climate change seriously and build energy wisely.” [Read her article](https://www.aspendailynews.com/opinion/thank-you-core-for-helping-at-stott-s-mill/article_62c8a89a-77fb-11ef-a823-2b1d8ec67b21.html) in the Aspen Daily News.

###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)

By Julie Kapala • November 9, 2025
Learn how a nonprofit overcame floodplain and zoning challenges to build a sustainable healing center that sets a new standard for green construction.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

#  **This February: Opening our Doors and Raising the Bar**  

Last night, we hosted an open house at our newly renovated office in Basalt and were so energized by the turnout. Seeing our partners, supporters, and community members gathered together was a meaningful way to celebrate how we’ve grown. This new space gives our expanding team the room and resources to better serve our community and advance local climate solutions together.
  

At the event, we recognized Atlantic Aviation for renewing its generous challenge grant for 2026. This commitment increases the impact of every donation by 50%, helping your support go even further as we work to reduce emissions 20% more than we did in 2025.
  

﻿Thank you for your continued support of CORE’s mission and the meaningful climate work happening across our region.
  

Sincerely,
  

[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed-1920w.png)](https://www.aspencore.org/tara-stitzlein)

#  CORE'S 2025 Impact Report﻿
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/2025-Impact-Report-Cover_cropped_page-0001-1920w.png)](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/2025_CORE_Impact+Report.pdf)
Last year, CORE provided $2.5 million in grants and rebates to support 213 home and business energy efficiency and electrification projects across Pitkin, Garfield, and Eagle Counties. CORE also hosted its first-ever Green Expo, bringing hundreds of local residents and businesses together, and expanded our team to better serve the community's needs.
Explore the 2025 Impact Report to see key results, community success stories, donor recognition, and our goals for 2026.
[**Read the full 2025 Impact Report**](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/files/uploaded/2025_CORE_Impact+Report.pdf)**→**
  

* * *
# Celebrating Our Renovated Basalt Office
After several months of construction, CORE's newly renovated Basalt office is officially open. Yesterday's open house brought familiar faces, new connections, and great conversations about CORE's ambitious plans for 2026. With office renovations complete, CORE is excited to be working with the building owners, Harry Teague Architects, and Basalt River Lofts HOA, to upgrade the building's mechanical system. With assistance from CORE and Holy Cross, the natural gas boilers that heat the building will be replaced with cold-climate air-to-water heat pumps to improve energy efficiency and indoor/outdoor air quality.
  

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/CORE_OpenHouse_Collage_v5-1920w.jpg)
* * *
# Own or Manage a Commercial or
#  Multifamily Building in Eagle County?  

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%288%29-1920w.jpg)
New in 2026, CORE's commercial and multifamily programming is now available throughout all of Eagle County, from Vail to Basalt. If you own, manage, or are a part of an HOA for a commercial property or a multifamily building with four or more units, you can access free energy assessments, expert energy advising, and up to $200,000 in grants and rebates for energy efficiency and electrification projects. Commercial and multifamily buildings have the potential to make the biggest impact on reducing greenhouse gas emissions and reaching our climate action goals.
[**Learn more about eligible commercial and multifamily energy efficiency projects**](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding).
* * *
# You Met the Match & It's Back for 2026
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Atlantic+Aviation-1920w.png)
In 2025, Atlantic Aviation generously stepped forward with a $300,000 challenge grant, which inspired $600,000 in donations, for a total impact of $900,000 in philanthropic support for CORE. Given that success, Atlantic Aviation is renewing its commitment for 2026, and all donations to CORE this year will once again have a 1.5 multiplier.
  

"The community’s ability to meet our 2025 challenge grant speaks to the credibility that CORE carries and the value it delivers across the community. That success and our shared commitment made renewing Atlantic Aviation’s challenge grant for 2026 an easy decision. We are proud to continue this partnership and accelerate practical, on-the-ground climate action across the Roaring Fork Valley." – Jonathan Jones, General Manager, Atlantic Aviation
  

[**Make a matched gift here**](https://www.aspencore.org/donate) →
  

* * *
#  Stop Losing Heat Every Winter
If your home or building is drafty, you could be losing heat and money all winter. To identify solutions, contact CORE to set up a home energy assessment. After an assessment, a CORE Energy Concierge will help you make a plan to improve the energy efficiency of your home through upgrades like air sealing, insulation, or heat pumps. CORE funding helps make improvements more affordable across Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield Counties.
  

Rebates for homes up to $10,000  
Grants for businesses up to $200,000
  

Home energy assessments are FREE for community priority participants and $100 for all other residences.
  

Upgrade once. Save every winter.
﻿
[**Schedule your energy assessment**](https://energysmartcolorado.formstack.com/forms/residential_enrollment)**→**
  

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/e191040d-a857-403b-9a92-b352691d875e-1920w.png)

Gina McCrackin

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Gina-McCrackin-CORE-Staff-1920w.png)
### Gina McCrackin
Director of Regional Strategy
* * *
Gina grew up in Metro Detroit, Michigan and discovered her passion for solving social and environmental problems by bearing witness to the Flint Michigan Water Crisis. She moved to Colorado and received her B.S. in Human Dimensions of Natural Resources from Colorado State University, where she served as the Director of Environmental Affairs for her student government. 
  
Graduate school pursuits brought Gina to Utah State University, where she received her M.S. in Environmental Sociology. She had the honor to learn from the Northwestern Band of the Shoshone Nation as she researched how Indigenous and Western communities are discussing climate change differently.
  
At CORE, Gina facilitates climate action initiatives in the built environment and beyond for the Eagle, Pitkin, and Garfield County region. She supports local governments in their building code planning, adoption, and implementation efforts, and provides expert advisory to the region on aligned climate action efforts. Gina’s knowledge and skillsets are vast, with most of her experience being in buildings and transportation decarbonization initiatives. Gina is skilled at facilitation, leading planning efforts, program and policy development and implementation, and grant management. 
  
In Gina’s free time, you can find her hiking, camping, or skiing outdoors, in her garden, at a bluegrass concert, or sunbathing with her two cats, Merry and Pippin.   

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
970.925.9775 x 1004  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
gina@aspencore.org

# Federal and State Tax Programs Sweeten the Deal on Home Energy Improvements
February 25, 2025
## Maximize Your Tax Refund with Energy-Saving Rebates  

Originally published: February 29, 2024
Updated: February 29, 2025
  
Tax Day is April 15, and whether you have already filed or are still pulling receipts together, it’s nice to know what tax breaks could help you save - both dollars and the planet. 
  
The 2022 [Inflation Reduction Act](https://www.irs.gov/credits-deductions/clean-vehicle-and-energy-credits) allocates $370 billion towards supporting consumers and industry partners in advancing - and paying for - climate action initiatives. More than $8 billion of those funds are intended to go towards funding home energy credits. In 2024, [2.3 million families received more than $2 billion in energy efficiency tax credits](https://www.energystar.gov/products/ask-the-experts/federal-tax-credits-energy-efficiency-2025-what-you-need-know), averaging $880 per family.
  
The State of Colorado offers additional tax incentives to Coloradans, including clean energy tax credits for [electric vehicles](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/transportation/grants-incentives/electric-vehicle-tax-credits), [e-bikes](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/ebike-tax-credit), [industrial improvements](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/citco), and [electric lawn and garden equipment](https://tax.colorado.gov/electric-powered-lawn-equipment-tax-credit).
  
So, how do you get a piece of the pie while decreasing your carbon footprint? Let’s dig in. 
**  
For those who own homes.**
  
When it comes to energy saving in the home, [federal](https://www.energy.gov/policy/articles/making-our-homes-more-efficient-clean-energy-tax-credits-consumers) and [state](https://energysmartcolorado.org/tax-credits-incentives/#:~:text=The%2025C%20Tax%20Credit%20\(previously,cap%20of%20%24600%20per%20measure%20\() tax incentives predominantly apply to those who own the property. Many of the rebates offer up to 30% of the original cost of the equipment, including things like:
  * Heat pumps
  * Solar
  * Battery storage
  * Air conditioners
  * Insulation
  * Exterior windows and doors


  
Looking for more ways to save? Local utility providers like [Black Hills Energy](https://www.blackhillsenergy.com/efficiency-and-savings/residential-rebates/colorado-gas-residential-rebates) and [Holy Cross Energy](https://www.holycross.com/rebates/) offer energy efficiency rebate programs. Additionally, you may qualify for [CORE’s rebates and incentives for residential and commercial projects.](https://www.aspencore.org/savings-finder)
**  
What if I don’t own property?**
  
If you don’t own your home, you won’t be eligible for many of the property improvement rebates. But do not fret! There are still a lot of ways you can save energy in your home, resulting in dollars saved.
  
To start your energy-saving journey, take a hard look at your lighting sources. Since [lighting accounts for 11% of energy use in the typical home](https://www.energy.gov/energysaver/why-energy-efficiency-upgrades), reduce your light energy by [switching to LEDs](https://www.energystar.gov/products/learn-about-led-lighting). They provide a higher quality of light, use 75% less energy, and have a longer lifespan. While incandescent bulbs last for 1,000 hours and compact fluorescent lamps (CFLs) for 10,000 hours, LEDs last up to 25,000 hours or more. Make sure you recycle CFLs, which contain mercury, at the [Pitkin County Landfill.](https://pitkincounty.com/488/Landfill)
  
You can also install lighting controls, such as timers, occupancy sensors, and daylighting controls that are designed to only put light out when and where you need it most. 
  
A few other ideas for reducing energy usage in the home include: 
  * Wash your clothes in cold water.
  * Take a bite out of vampire loads and plug electronics into an [advanced power strip](https://science.howstuffworks.com/environmental/green-tech/sustainable/smart-power-strip.htm). 
  * Grab a sweater and turn down the heat. 
  * Using wool dryer balls can reduce dry time by providing clothes with more air, reducing static, and absorbing moisture.


**  
Want to learn more?**[Schedule a home energy assessment](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-assessments) through CORE or your utility company, and then submit for up to $150 in a [federal rebate](https://www.energy.gov/policy/articles/making-our-homes-more-efficient-clean-energy-tax-credits-consumers) to cover some of the cost. 
  
Energy reduction savings for federal and state tax incentives span beyond properties to mobility, as well. Explore other credits and rebates available for purchases of electric vehicles, bikes, and mowers - to name a few. 
  
If you have questions about navigating the deep hole of tax rebates, check out our [website](https://www.aspencore.org/savings-finder) or schedule an appointment with our [Energy Concierge](https://aspencore.org/energy-concierge/) team. A qualified tax specialist can also help you find and navigate [federal](https://www.irs.gov/credits-deductions/home-energy-tax-credits) and [state](https://tax.colorado.gov/individual-income-tax-forms) tax forms and additional resources. 
**  
Future Savings**
  
If you didn’t pull the plug on doing energy upgrades last year, you can still benefit from tax savings. More funding is available and will continue to be released this year and years to follow. Follow [CORE](https://www.aspencore.org/), the [Colorado Energy Office](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/), and the [US Department of Energy](https://www.energy.gov/policy/articles/making-our-homes-more-efficient-clean-energy-tax-credits-consumers) for more information.   

* * *
This content is proudly included in the [Randy Udall Memorial Educational Program](https://www.aspencore.org/events), advancing energy education and climate action.  

[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Coerdert+Case+Study+%281%29-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
###  [Building a Zero-Emissions Healing Center in Colorado](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
By Julie Kapala • November 9, 2025
Learn how a nonprofit overcame floodplain and zoning challenges to build a sustainable healing center that sets a new standard for green construction.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

Just beyond the Downtown Core lies Smuggler Park, a fabled Aspen subdivision the HOA says is made up of “real homes for real locals.” Two of those locals, Sam and Desi Barney, are using a CORE grant to drive real change when it comes to how their home uses energy.

###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)

**About CORE**
CORE is a 501(c)(3) nonprofit organization urgently reducing carbon emissions through optimizing efficiency, electrification, and resiliency of the built environment, while advancing innovative climate-saving solutions.

**GreenPower Motors:** Quiet, zero-emission, and built for community transport – the EV Star Passenger van will be on display at CORE’s Green Expo. Stop by to explore fleet electrification solutions and upcoming Colorado incentives to support fleet electrification.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/GreenPower-MOTOR-COMPANY-1920w.png)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/atlantic-logo-4c-cntr-blue-1920w.png)
**Atlantic Aviation** is an aviation infrastructure operator offering customers more than 100 fixed base operation (FBO) locations across North America and is the FBO provider that supports aviation activities locally at Aspen / Pitkin County Airport. At Atlantic, our mission is to be a visible leader in general aviation's journey toward environmental stewardship, sustainability, and responsibility. We make real, pragmatic investments in our facilities, equipment, and systems to drive year over year improvements. And we're committed to empowering our partners and customers to make similar progress through innovative, sustainable solutions.
**American Plumbing Heating Cooling & Electrical ** proudly serves the Roaring Fork and Vail Valleys with expert residential and commercial solutions. We specialize in high efficiency HVAC systems, plumbing, and licensed electrical work, delivering quality, sustainability, and long-term performance. Our team is committed to keeping homes and businesses safe, efficient, and running smoothly year round.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/American+Plumbing-1920w.jpg)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Sunsense-1920w.png)
**Sunsense:** Celebrating 35 years in the solar electric and energy storage business, Sunsense has grown into one of the premier solar electric Engineering, Procurement and Construction (EPC) contractors in Colorado. Sunsense provides turnkey services for solar electric and energy storage systems of all sizes and specifications to a broad array of clients. The Sunsense goal is to proactively continue building a long-term, sustainable business based on quality, credibility and service to our clients.
**Spice it Up:** Susie Jimenez is a nationally recognized chef and TV personality known for her bold flavors and energetic style, rising to fame as a finalist on Food Network Star. She has cooked for celebrities, appeared on major food and lifestyle shows, and contributes to culinary media across platforms. Beyond the kitchen, Susie is a passionate community advocate, supporting causes like autism education and child abuse prevention.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Spice+it+up-1920w.png)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Full+Circle-1920w.jpg)
**Full Circle Construction Services** helps builders, architects, and homeowners create comfortable, energy-efficient spaces—without the guesswork. Our Aeroseal duct sealing technology stops leaky ducts from the inside out, improving comfort, indoor air quality, and system performance while cutting energy costs. We also provide HERS ratings, blower door testing, and energy consulting to ensure your project is sealed tight and performing right.
**Littell Electric:** Littell Electric specializes in creating energy-efficient environments through modern lighting, automation, and shading solutions. By combining advanced technology with smart design, we help reduce energy use while enhancing comfort and control. Our mission is to make a lasting impact by shaping homes and businesses that are both sustainable and future-ready.
![](https://irp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/LittellElectric.gif)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Delta+Brick+-+Climate+Company-1920w.jpg)
**Delta Brick & Climate Company** works to destroy methane leaking from abandoned coal mines in Colorado. They have partnered with CORE on the Coal Basin Methane Project to address emissions from the mines near Redstone. Delta Brick's sister company, Particular Tile, handmakes sustainable tile using the mud clogging Paonia Reservoir.
**Holy Cross Energy:** Founded in 1939, Holy Cross Energy (HCE) is a not-for-profit rural electric co-op providing safe, reliable, affordable, and sustainable energy and services that improve the quality of life for more than 45,000 members in western Colorado. HCE was built by and belongs to the diverse communities and members we serve. Membership is open to everyone in our service territory, regardless of race, religion, age, disability, language, political perspective, or socioeconomic status. HCE is committed to leading the responsible transition to a clean energy future with a goal of safely providing 100% clean, affordable and reliable energy to its members by 2030.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HCE_Color_2023--281-29-1920w.png)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/City+of+Aspen-1920w.png)
**City of Aspen:** The City of Aspen’s Environmental Health and Sustainability Department aims to protect and nurture an equitable, healthy, and resilient community and environment through partnership, purposeful service, and innovative action. The health of our community and environment is what makes Aspen such a special place. We dedicate our work to ensuring that the local environment, members of our community, and visitors thrive now and into the future. The City of Aspen works through policy, programs, and partnership to reach the City’s ambitious climate action goals and to implement the Aspen Sustainability Action Plan.
**Mountain Air Mechanical:** Mountain Air Mechanical is a HVAC contractor that has been in business since 2002. We specialize in providing energy efficient heating and cooling options to homes and businesses in the Roaring Fork Valley. Our goal is to make your comfort a priority with cost, sustainability, and energy savings in mind.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Mountain-Air-Mechanical-1920w.png)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Powder+Watts-1920w.png)
**Powder Watts:** Designed to endure the harshest winter environments, our WiFi-enabled Powder Watts smart cameras reduce heat cable energy demands by 70-90%, returning upfront investment for residential and commercial buildings in 1-2 years. We are excited to offer both virtual and in-person installer trainings this fall in Pitkin County!

January 2026 Newsletter

#  This January: Setting Goals & Embracing Challenges  

**This January: Setting Goals & Embracing Challenges**
As we begin a new year, I am embracing challenges as opportunities. Our goals are ambitious, and our team is prepared:
  

  * Increase emissions reduction impact by 20% over 2025
  * Continue to award at least 40% of our incentives to under-resourced members of our community
  * Build stronger regional partnerships to unlock greater impact and funding opportunities
  * Deliver expert energy advising backed by grants and rebates for all community members
  * Continue to increase philanthropic support to ensure sustainable growth


  

My commitment remains unwavering: making climate solutions accessible to everyone in our region. Thank you for your partnership in this vital work. Together, we empower our local communities to embrace energy efficiency and electrification, creating a healthier environment for all.
﻿
Sincerely,
  

[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed-1920w.png)](https://www.aspencore.org/tara-stitzlein)
* * *
# Welcome to the Team: Sam Johnston
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/CORE-Staff-Sam-Johnston-c5839de4-1920w.png)](https://www.aspencore.org/sam-johnston)
Meet CORE's newest Energy Concierge for residential programs! [**Sam Johnston**](https://www.aspencore.org/sam-johnston) is a Basalt native and recent CU Boulder graduate with degrees in Environmental Studies and Sociology. Sam brings deep community roots and fresh passion to CORE. In her role, she will help local residents navigate home energy upgrades, electrification, and rebate programs to reduce greenhouse gas emissions. When Sam's not making energy efficiency accessible for our neighbors, you'll find her skiing Snowmass, baking, or hiking near Ruedi Reservoir.
[ Meet Sam Johnston ](https://www.aspencore.org/sam-johnston)
#  Don't Let Your Heating Bills Melt Your Budget﻿
If your heat is escaping, so is your money. Drafty homes and buildings and inefficient heating systems drive up bills and harm our mountain environment.
  

CORE can help with energy audits, insulation upgrades, heat pumps, and more. In 2026, homeowners can access up to $15,000 in rebates, while businesses qualify for up to $50,000.
  

Energy assessments are completely free for [Community Priority Participants.](https://www.aspencore.org/community-priority-participants) Whether you rent or own, now's the perfect time to start saving! 
[ Get an Energy Assement ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-assessments)
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/191108jk-energysmart-029-1920w.jpg)](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-assessments)
* * *
# Energy Spotlight: Old Snowmass Homeowners
#  Build Back After Fire﻿
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/b33630d0-2db6-4421-9fb9-840fcce9f2cc-1920w.jpeg)](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
When a catastrophic fire destroyed [**Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home**](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience-how-one-colorado-couple-created-an-all-electric-solar-powered-home-after-devastating-fire) in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. Their new 3,400-square-foot home produces most of its own clean energy, eliminates fossil fuels entirely, and costs a fraction of typical homes to operate. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living, and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
  

[ Read More ](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
* * *
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Energy+Smart+Colorado-1920w.png)
# CORE CEO Joins ESC Board of Directors
  

﻿Congratulations to CORE's CEO, Tara Stitzlein, on being appointed to the [**Energy Smart Colorado**](https://energysmartcolorado.org/) (ESC) Board of Directors! This appointment comes full circle: CORE was a founding partner of ESC 15 years ago. Today, ESC is a collaboration of community partners serving 20 Colorado counties, making energy efficiency improvements simple and affordable. Tara joins other regional climate leaders in guiding this vital organization that shares resources and builds capacity across Colorado's clean energy landscape.
* * *
#  Join CORE on February 1 at the Full Moon Dinner  

Meet the CORE team at the[**Full Moon Dinner at Cliffhouse on February 1**](https://www.aspensnowmass.com/visit/events/full-moon-dinners-at-the-cliffhouse). Stop by our table and discover how we can partner on energy efficiency and electrification projects for your home or business. We'll have swag, flyers, and a fun game with prizes. Skin or hike up Buttermilk's Main route for this monthly celebration beneath the illuminated winter sky. Enjoy the cash bar, delicious dinner options, and live music from local musicians.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/cf212dab-6a07-47ba-a033-d01956830508-1920w.png)

Julia Wilson

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/CORE-Staff-Julia-Wilson-df86902d-1920w.png)
### Julia Wilson
Julia Wilson, Programs Manager
* * *
Julia developed both a deep relationship with the land and a talent for creative problem solving growing up on a fifth generation family farm in the Ozarks. She brings experience partnering with utilities on the research and design of customer programs and digital tools to reduce peak demand and expand the use of clean energy.
  
Julia has a B.S. in Electrical Engineering from the University of Missouri and began her career as an industrial engineer in oil fields and gas processing plants. She then moved from operations to research after earning an M.S. in Environmental Science from the University of Colorado, working in atmospheric CO2 modeling with the Long Term Ecological Research Network and leading early studies of mountain pine beetle impact in Colorado. Julia later moved into education teaching creative problem solving in the Engineering, Design and Society department at the Colorado School of Mines. 
  
Julia is a jazz/blues vocalist performing with various music groups and loves paddling lakes in her kayak. She is pursuing certification as a Nature and Forest Therapy Guide and loves helping people discover the mental health benefits of connecting with the natural world.  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
970.925.9775 x 1009  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
julia@aspencore.org

July 2025 Newsletter
* * *
### July CORE Updates: Events & Summer Rebate Special
###  Friends of CORE,   

Summer in the Roaring Fork Valley is a powerful reminder of what we’re working to protect and what’s possible when our community comes together.  
  
From local nonprofits going all-electric to regional partnerships that move the needle on climate, your engagement is what makes this work possible.  
  
Thank you for being part of the momentum.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Screenshot+2025-08-25+at+4.52.33+PM-1920w.png)
**John Dougherty  
**
**Chief Executive Officer, CORE**  

P.S. Keep scrolling for exciting updates—from a brand-new all-electric community center to bonus summer rebates and upcoming events across the valley. There's real progress happening and we’d love for you to be part of it!
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/green+expo-1920w.png)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/NPG05233-302f9db2-1920w.jpg)
Join CORE on September 12th for an afternoon designed to inspire and accelerate climate action in our community. With engaging presentations, hands-on demonstrations, and networking opportunities, the Green Expo is ideal for anyone curious about practical ways to make a climate impact. **FREE & open to the public, but space is limited! **

# Summer Special:  
Bonus Rebates Are Here
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/photo+collage+%281%29-1920w.png)
Starting July 20, CORE is offering limited-time bonus rebates for energy upgrades in Eagle, Pitkin, and Garfield counties, available **through October 20**.
  

Homeowners, businesses, and multifamily properties can receive an **additional $500** for energy efficiency improvements including air sealing, insulation, and controls, and an **extra $1,000** for fuel-switching projects such as installing heat pumps. In total, rebates can now cover **up to 60%** of project costs.
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/example+savings+%281%29-1920w.png)
[ Apply For Rebates Today! ](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-and-local-funding-programs)
### Project Spotlight: English in Action
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/project-spotlight-1920w.jpg)
CORE awarded $40,000 to English in Action to help build their new all-electric, energy-efficient community center. This vital nonprofit connects volunteers with immigrants through English learning and mentorship. Their new space now welcomes 700+ community members into a safe, inclusive, and climate-conscious home.
  

**Thinking about your own project?**

**About CORE**
CORE is a 501(c)(3) nonprofit organization urgently reducing carbon emissions through optimizing efficiency, electrification, and resiliency of the built environment, while advancing innovative climate-saving solutions.

### Energy Spotlight: 
### The Fire Place - Housing Our Heroes
Aspen Fire District’s All-Electric Workforce Housing
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%287%29-1920w.jpg)
Battalion Chief Ken Josselyn gives a tour of an all-electric home in the Fire Place.
When our first responders are ready to answer the call, they shouldn't have to worry about where they'll sleep at night. That's the thinking behind "The Fire Place," the Aspen Fire District’s workforce housing project that's changing how we support our essential workers.
Starting in 2022, the Aspen Fire District partnered with CORE to advise and fund this all-electric multifamily housing complex in the AABC. The fifteen safe, modern, and comfortable homes are located right next door to the fire station, giving our firefighters the ultimate short commute while ensuring they're close when emergencies arise.
Each unit features state-of-the-art amenities that prioritize both comfort and efficiency: heat pumps for year-round climate control, ENERGY STAR appliances, LED lighting throughout, and programmable thermostats. These aren't just energy-efficient features; they're quality-of-life improvements that help our essential workers focus on what matters most: keeping our community safe.
The Fire Place represents more than just housing; it's a commitment to the people who serve our community every day and showcases what's possible when local agencies work together to solve real community challenges. The Fire Place proves that workforce housing can be both sustainable and supportive of those who serve us all.
**Ready to upgrade your building project? CORE offers up to $200K for energy-saving commercial and multifamily projects.**
[ Learn More ](https://www.aspencore.org/commercial-multifamily-funding)
* * *
### CORE & Eagle County Are Stepping up to Help Building Owners Meet State Standards
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%288%29-1920w.jpg)
CORE assesses building operation systems to help identify areas of improvement.
Colorado's [new energy standards](https://energyoffice.colorado.gov/bpc?blm_aid=13313) require buildings 50,000 square feet and larger to reduce carbon emissions. CORE and Eagle County are working together to help buildings in Eagle County turn this compliance challenge into a competitive advantage. 
In addition to helping property owners avoid state penalties, CORE can provide FREE services to help tackle deferred maintenance, boost property value, and cut operating costs.
[ Contact CORE To Get Started ](https://www.aspencore.org/eagle-county-building-performance)
* * *
### Save the Date - September 12, 2025
#### Green Expo Spotlights Climate Solutions
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%289%29-1920w.jpg)
Green Expo attendees can talk with vendors and test sustainable technology, like this all-electric snowblower.
Ready to turn bright ideas into real-world action? Save the date for an inspiring afternoon that will change how you see sustainability. The Green Expo, presented by CORE, is on September 12 at the Limelight Aspen. 
At the Green Expo, you’ll hear from local champions and global innovators who are making real progress on climate solutions. You’ll discover practical tools and simple steps that you can take right now to lower your carbon footprint and save money, whether you’re a homeowner, a business leader, or just someone who wants to do more.
This event is FREE to attend and open to the public.
Registration opens August 1.
[ Learn More ](https://www.aspencore.org/green-expo)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%284%29-1920w.png)

Kate Lamair
* * *
![Kate Lamair with Aspen CORE](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/_pzon27w64jXMagejgfaQYnpPjlB4WNSJNbeB9WopT4-1920w.png)
### Kate LaMair
Development Coordinator  

* * *
The Rocky Mountains are where Kate discovered her love for nature and, eventually, her desire to devote her career to protecting the future of our climate and communities. Kate earned her bachelor’s degree in psychology and sociology from the University of Colorado Boulder and went on to complete her master’s degree in Environmental Policy and Management from the University of Denver.
  

Between her studies, Kate found herself far from home, working as an outdoor guide in Hong Kong, studying and teaching yoga in India, volunteering in Indonesia, and conducting research in Puerto Rico. Throughout her education, travels, and a year-long internship at the National Renewable Energy Laboratory (NREL), Kate developed a passion for empowering grassroots efforts to combat the climate crisis and support the energy transition.
  

For her final capstone project in graduate school, she researched community engagement as a key strategy for designing and implementing energy transitions that promote environmental and social justice.
  

In her new role at CORE, Kate’s goal is to make her vision a reality by getting her hands dirty in the grassroots efforts our region and contributing to a better future for our precious natural areas and beloved communities. When she’s not in the office, Kate is most likely found on top of a mountain, in the yoga studio, or at a Billy Strings show.  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
970-230-5873  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
Kate@AspenCORE.org

Kimberly Marcum
* * *
![Kimberly Marcum](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/XZof0L7v-1920w.png)
### Kimberly Marcum
Marketing & Community Engagement Coordinator
* * *
Kimberly Marcum leads marketing and community engagement at CORE, where she focuses on turning complex ideas about energy, buildings, and electrification into something people can actually understand—and use. She is especially drawn to work that directly improves people’s day-to-day lives and values being part of work that shows up locally and actually makes a difference.
  

Her work sits at the intersection of communication, community, and climate, helping residents, businesses, and partners connect with practical tools that reduce energy use and support a healthier Roaring Fork Valley. She is particularly interested in the moment when information turns into action—whether through a conversation, a community event, or a campaign that finally makes something click.
  

Kimberly’s background is rooted in Colorado’s mountain communities, where she led marketing for destination-based organizations and developed a strong appreciation for the balance between vibrant local economies and responsible stewardship. That perspective traces back to her early work in wildlife education at the Louisville Zoo in Kentucky, where she spent time in the bird blind on the surrounding parkland, helping visitors connect more closely with local wildlife and ecosystems.
  

Outside of work, Kimberly splits her time between hot springs, hiking, and ongoing home projects that are never quite finished. She reads a mix of history and philosophy, keeps more plants than she probably needs, and shares her home with a small gang of cats.  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
[970.925.9775 x1012](tel:\(970\)%20925-9775)
A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
kimberly@aspencore.org

* * *
Lee Macke
* * *
![Lee has his hair pulled back, is wearing a red shirt, and is standing in front of a river. ](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC02309--281-29-1920w.jpg)
### Lee Macke
Project Manager
* * *
Lee brings over a decade of experience in energy performance contracting and a deep background in sustainable construction to his role at CORE. A mechanical engineering graduate of Georgia Tech, he has helped build everything from schools and libraries to clinics and cabins, most recently focusing on energy efficiency projects across the western and midwestern United States.
  

Originally from the South, Lee’s path has included stints as a cook, a line chef at a snow cat-accessed restaurant in Vail, and a builder of LEED-certified projects in Colorado’s mountain communities. He’s passionate about how buildings work and how they can work better. When he’s not at work, you’ll find him mountain biking, splitboarding, or exploring the outdoors with his son and daughter, often near the off-grid cabin he built up Independence Pass.  
  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
1-970-925-9775 x 1010  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
Lee@AspenCORE.org

* * *
March 2026 Newsletter
* * *
###  **In the News: Building Momentum Across Our Region**  

I shared in our recent Aspen Times feature that, “in the midst of a challenging year for climate work in general, we’re really grateful and inspired that we saw the success that we did and that we were able to inspire our community to look at what they can do to contribute to climate action.” In 2025, CORE supported more than 200 projects in local buildings and made meaningful reductions in carbon emissions across our region. What’s most encouraging is what this momentum represents. Each project is a commitment—by building owners, contractors, and partners—to practical, local solutions that will reshape our communities and create a better future.
  

﻿This year, we are building on those commitments to accelerate our progress on impactful climate solutions. Atlantic Aviation’s continued partnership through its challenge grant and the contributions of all of our generous donors equip us with the resources to be responsive to the needs of our region, multiply the impact of local government funding, and enable CORE to expand to serve new communities.
  

Thank you for your continued support of CORE’s mission and for your role in the meaningful work happening across our region.
Sincerely,
  

[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed-1920w.png)](https://www.aspencore.org/tara-stitzlein)
* * *

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC00223+%281%29-1920w.JPG)
CORE is showing up for Earth Day twice. # CORE in the News:
#  Record Year for Emissions Reduction Work﻿
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/aspentimes+news-1920w.jpg)](https://www.aspentimes.com/news/pitkin-countys-climate-nonprofit-reports-record-breaking-year/?blm_aid=0)
A recent Aspen Times feature takes a closer look at CORE’s record-breaking year and growing impact across the region. With more than 200 projects completed and measurable reductions in carbon emissions, the story reflects a steady shift toward more efficient, all-electric buildings in the Roaring Fork Valley.
﻿
Read the entire article [HERE.](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrXhzYR2Eq9VlF-2Fd2rIWb-2BkKrritRBX0breZObrKtQgVvn2XygL0StZAHzHT-2B0iHo9jqApkQ3Emkw6v051wCzEzYD97ckmTB5T71CrVRxNS73zkv2bRqFTR1QgjfIu8lp9YTGsXnKlhQhVRypm7rkp-2FU-3Db21z_pLkck-2B6Kp8XQahTtHIyzW72MowB5OhXXkfUaEtey2p3DAbIog5XP0z5-2BgQrhpYgicqJdmsG-2Fs-2FystY0N0GSo-2FCUjQy3TFQjb8-2B9Q-2BN-2BPq1DQAAyb0DNX5yVSoK1Mi4PvCpK6HhT-2FplFtoXxQ638tCu73AHpihU0qZbabPzwVjYir7wASYORvJ1g1fvaC4AKwZ0NJNRhijaABrWP4dMIOQg-3D-3D)
  

You can also explore the data for yourself in our [2025 Impact Report](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrd-2FfEiUxs1P6NCPPpXXzSQEpzf-2BnolqQ9Iy0xsh00M8Xmw4cgqNR6ilPXLncbUNjkNkNeyXCpz9bkkVrjaVaBlZleZTKbCdJKq94od6-2FX6ouooNDWLArtsE7aojQBVSM7Q-3D-3DD6sU_pLkck-2B6Kp8XQahTtHIyzW72MowB5OhXXkfUaEtey2p3DAbIog5XP0z5-2BgQrhpYgicqJdmsG-2Fs-2FystY0N0GSo-2FFnJr5C1od76Lpp9xGOEnnhSEkugIFjlwbQeR6xrShpW-2BcUQtcPXo1R31w8qNORWEuHfm1xEv9RiFpz0zaZildy9o0i0DbtZxVpaawjz1cmGhCrsadQPXfmKSXhGR35wpA-3D-3D).

# A Better Way to Talk About Energy
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/202512_CORE_Toolkit-1920w.png)
The [CORE Energy Messaging](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrd-2FfEiUxs1P6NCPPpXXzSQEpzf-2BnolqQ9Iy0xsh00M8XS4vtUgUzp9HP7UmR43e-2BD2ovQfSHYxqBkPoV8z-2FE9S-2B3fTJnWjDhhvENi-2BBsZooHhY95YctExzCVE5J-2BxBB2Eg-3D-3DyQJF_pLkck-2B6Kp8XQahTtHIyzW72MowB5OhXXkfUaEtey2p3DAbIog5XP0z5-2BgQrhpYgicqJdmsG-2Fs-2FystY0N0GSo-2FLTP0eLLxN0RAkWuOyYNQtjYLDbsSoL1SONmz-2BNjf8dYj6IljvgtjB8NCAjLAGxtBdFGARCf-2B4BQ9M0y9hU6QTNjvNocDNS-2B4HwJrRxSkK6RvnuaIasRbfHO9vNbsKQMvw-3D-3D)[ Toolkit](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrd-2FfEiUxs1P6NCPPpXXzSQEpzf-2BnolqQ9Iy0xsh00M8XS4vtUgUzp9HP7UmR43e-2BD2ovQfSHYxqBkPoV8z-2FE9S-2B3fTJnWjDhhvENi-2BBsZooHhY95YctExzCVE5J-2BxBB2Eg-3D-3DkrHE_pLkck-2B6Kp8XQahTtHIyzW72MowB5OhXXkfUaEtey2p3DAbIog5XP0z5-2BgQrhpYgicqJdmsG-2Fs-2FystY0N0GSo-2FByIP1DmUCFiQaxgz43cNdgb0VkN-2F-2FJztZLRErWwxZpSjGxDSdpQ7DhRHA1CiDoVfSqCONsdeirgxw-2FCDgJxxUi3-2FRU1fle594XrhlRdRy162aQao5OVFyiNXNS1LFqVSw-3D-3D) is designed for local governments, community partners, and organizations working to communicate about building efficiency, electrification, and emissions reduction.
Clear, consistent messaging plays a critical role in how energy decisions are understood and adopted. This resource provides practical guidance for translating complex topics into communication that resonates with residents, businesses, and industry professionals.
For those shaping conversations around energy in the community, this toolkit offers a valuable starting point.
**Explore the toolkit →**[**Download**](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrd-2FfEiUxs1P6NCPPpXXzSQEpzf-2BnolqQ9Iy0xsh00M8XS4vtUgUzp9HP7UmR43e-2BD2ovQfSHYxqBkPoV8z-2FE9S-2B3fTJnWjDhhvENi-2BBsZooHhY95YctExzCVE5J-2BxBB2Eg-3D-3D1kf__pLkck-2B6Kp8XQahTtHIyzW72MowB5OhXXkfUaEtey2p3DAbIog5XP0z5-2BgQrhpYgicqJdmsG-2Fs-2FystY0N0GSo-2FBdWysQdWOoVZez2FjjeKddvU5A-2BrVw7QN-2FoxpH1Pfv-2BkCL6nFJbXLkRTnGki0faHcciAEflMCNF6TkeEaU9SaZ0FeSDfAfnYAiuBWo20lt1qa8mo8ch8fymGMvdsQnm2g-3D-3D)

## Welcome to the Team: Kimberly Marcum
[![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/XZof0L7v-1920w.png)](https://www.aspencore.org/kimberly-marcum)
Kimberly Marcum is CORE’s Marketing & Community Engagement Coordinator, focused on shaping clear, accessible messaging around energy and building topics. Her work supports CORE’s communications and campaigns, helping connect the community with information and resources in an easy-to-understand, engaging way.
[ Meet Kimberly Marcum ](https://www.aspencore.org/kimberly-marcum)

October 2025 Newsletter

###  This October: Fall Brings Action & Inspiration  

As Fall settles into the Roaring Fork Valley, I’m reflecting on the power of community, collaboration, and what we can achieve when we come together. This month has been full of inspiration, from an event celebrating Indigenous youth paddling the restored Klamath River to stories of local homeowners transforming their energy use right here at home.
With the season of giving on the horizon, including [Colorado Gives Day](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrSJNy5WXOXpZ2ALTUUhPbEkh9gbysEOJHuSZaLgHjAC-2FshPZ8OjJAKxdn19HmsIERhFuJI81E6E70BR5FT8JOsHofSdzyifQk-2BRUiwJVbUoeWMGDys-2FMIcLIt-2BfeiHxpCw-3D-3D-2CA_-2B-2Bo8wEJrHrH-2BivbZZ1LDox7ql-2Ffc28b7Cj7YmWWqORyAVJUpvjmUUpB9Ylaka1qnMXC1ELxjpNdzoz-2BkDbkpdsIWMqtOCYS07AxiwtW46hmSHPm-2F3xNIAdWtJd0a5WlQVU3fYZcrt6-2BW66bmXjE8HzSt1ccsYUQJPPpnHG1FnTFzzmjebyGMHAdmLcUddMBh9G2lj44wyXonaN9jX9Zxhw-3D-3D)
  
on December 9, there are opportunities to multiply the impact of your donation and help CORE foster safer homes, cleaner air, and a more resilient community for all in the Roaring Fork Valley. 
  

Thank you for believing in our mission and for being an essential part of this journey.﻿
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%283%29-1920w.jpg)
### Ríos to Rivers & CORE Event Recap
Earlier this month, CORE co-hosted an inspiring evening with [Ríos to Rivers](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrVZAFeBlswcR-2F4y1rU3Iazc6wKBBRC7a7lD-2BjfXiqVAgw00qN1dLMO44WgX2SKzitQ-3D-3Dhr5Z_-2B-2Bo8wEJrHrH-2BivbZZ1LDox7ql-2Ffc28b7Cj7YmWWqORyAVJUpvjmUUpB9Ylaka1qnYNa5SxpJdHFyf5ixrR54-2FbqAEnsFh6lhas9QmBoi94PrIOrGu86hohYv5iCmdqwI1ir0yUR8Te-2BUYSrvgdnEkhpvSBzeIe9wD-2B-2B8MO20JEmZJBmS0jre1h9-2BQ8ofPqVBwaiFeuLcAyZ-2B4Xvu37pNAQ-3D-3D). Founder Weston Boyles shared how 120+ Indigenous youth paddled the restored Klamath River, celebrating dam removal and reclaimed lands. This 310-mile journey highlighted the power of collective action to drive meaningful progress in addressing the climate crisis across communities and generations.
[ View Event Photos ](https://www.facebook.com/ResourceEfficiency/posts/pfbid0APjt9FeC3mv7R23RSkrEw41QcLhiY8CJNeP8y4hLDVLwXtxrwBRDh6j2aLLsMiYgl?blm_aid=0)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%286%29-5b82c99a-1920w.png)
# **Energy Spotlight: The Osburn Family**
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%284%29-1920w.jpg)
Beth and Shannan Osburn transformed their 1980 mobile home in Lazy Glen with CORE’s support and Holy Cross Energy rebates covering 75% of costs. Step by step, they installed a heat pump, insulation, a programmable thermostat, an upgraded electrical panel, and more. Once challenged by temperature swings, their home now stays comfortable year-round with lower utility bills. Their journey proves how accessible energy upgrades can truly improve lives. 
  

**Are you ready to take the next step in improving your home?**
[ Calculate Your Energy Savings ](https://www.aspencore.org/federal-state-and-local-funding-programs)
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/unnamed+%285%29-1920w.jpg)
### Support CORE for Colorado Gives Day
Be part of the statewide giving movement! This [Colorado Gives Day](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrSJNy5WXOXpZ2ALTUUhPbEkh9gbysEOJHuSZaLgHjAC-2FshPZ8OjJAKxdn19HmsIERhFuJI81E6E70BR5FT8JOsHofSdzyifQk-2BRUiwJVbUoeWMGDys-2FMIcLIt-2BfeiHxpCw-3D-3D7L8w_-2B-2Bo8wEJrHrH-2BivbZZ1LDox7ql-2Ffc28b7Cj7YmWWqORyAVJUpvjmUUpB9Ylaka1qnJ2yBmfcUOEAXkxEAudIbj-2BlLGpb94RVA3m8T-2BUKfKUyj7NToIasDZ6QaBZBx1g5HwunI5GvWSvBcoDHsLQpslZhkaKAcM4I5Wptt2GOUO6KO4lVsSQkeWgm1w6-2BvpFgXlz-2B64uVI8Gl2QIyQK-2B5PqA-3D-3D), your donation to CORE creates triple the impact in three exciting ways:
  

1. **Early Giving Starts November 1** : From November 1 through December 9, every donation is boosted by a $1M+ Incentive Fund.
  

2. **Monthly Match** : Set up a new monthly recurring donation, and Colorado Gives Foundation will match your first gift up to $100.
  

3. **Atlantic Aviation Match** : Thanks to a generous grant CORE received from Atlantic Aviation, every dollar you contribute is matched by an additional 50%.
  

Every donation directly supports local climate action and helps reduce carbon emissions in the Roaring Fork Valley. Join thousands of Coloradans in this statewide wave of generosity. Every gift counts!﻿
[ Support CORE's Mission ](https://www.coloradogives.org/organization/Community-Office-For-Resource-Efficiency?blm_aid=0)
### **HOA Energy Upgrades Made Simple**
CORE’s free [**Energy Concierge**](https://u32723680.ct.sendgrid.net/ls/click?upn=u001.GxeCfx-2F3v4chiHts6ancrc6Wctj-2FtduGArh-2B-2BC5BC4Y5wrxJwhvUXTe1N7hFVFGgwUt7q9JWI08-2FheQaee-2BR-2FQ-3D-3DwIwN_-2B-2Bo8wEJrHrH-2BivbZZ1LDox7ql-2Ffc28b7Cj7YmWWqORyAVJUpvjmUUpB9Ylaka1qn2njw-2F0IqgTTnjUUgNsu6Py2AyuKzhpWMH7HayhEQmtHvr2xl9sN9OeygRLVvMnpPhCfO0PKgMnHEBUnwiMN3jIwjd2J-2B81JNhQXuy6GNW67LfSWKCl67S43yr8mmrpMfraLZynvlw7NYEDmf6zFdIA-3D-3D) simplifies energy upgrades for HOAs. We offer expert advice and connect you with rebates covering up to 50% of costs. Invite us to your HOA meeting to explore funding, technical support, and sustainability planning. Let us help you create safer, more efficient buildings while supporting local climate goals.

Ofek Bruhis
* * *
![Ofek is a blonde-haired man wearing a red shirt. Ofek is a project manager with CORE.](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/DSC02290-1f79a7f8-1920w.jpg)
### Ofek Bruhis
Project Manager
* * *
Ofek brings a strong foundation in sustainability and engineering to his role as a project manager with CORE. Prior to joining the team, he spent three and a half years working as a sustainability engineer, contributing to projects focused on energy efficiency, sustainable materials, LEED certification, greenhouse gas accounting, and climate-resilient building strategies. His technical background includes energy/carbon modeling, custom tool development for water and waste tracking, and active involvement in national efforts around responsible material sourcing.
  

Ofek earned his degrees in architectural engineering and applied mathematics from the University of Texas at Austin, where he also served as Head Engineer for the university’s Projects with Underserved Communities (PUC) program. There, he worked with a team to design a community center that served 78 families in rural India, an experience that shaped his passion for community-centered solutions.
  

Originally from Austin, Texas, Ofek moved to Colorado in 2021 after falling in love with the west during visits to spend time with family and friends. He’s an avid whitewater kayaker, one of four siblings (all now living in Colorado), and a volunteer goalie coach with Colorado Extreme, a nonprofit dedicated to youth development through hockey.
  

Outside of work, you’ll usually find Ofek chasing river flows. 
  
  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
1-970-925-9775 x 1001  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
Ofek@AspenCORE.org

# Randy Udall: A Pioneer in Climate Action (1951-2013)
December 5, 2024
#### **"Organize, don't agonize. [...] global warming will be a huge problem, one that won't disappear in our lifetimes. Some people will see this as an excuse to be apathetic--but it's really a call to action."**
#### **- Randy Udall, 1989**
Randy Udall was a visionary leader in the fight against climate change. He was CORE’s first executive director, and his efforts laid the foundation for transformative energy solutions across the Roaring Fork Valley and beyond. 
  

Known for his passion and foresight, Randy initiated Colorado’s first solar energy incentive program and co-founded the world’s first [Renewable Energy Mitigation Program](https://www.aspendailynews.com/news/the-outsized-impact-of-remp-residences/article_ceda8002-fcec-11ed-9be9-f38a300b83c6.html) (REMP) - a carbon fee model that has funded millions in local climate projects.
  

Before CORE, Randy was a freelance writer and environmental advocate. As early as 1987, he wrote about global warming’s emerging threats—melting glaciers, shrinking habitats, prolonged droughts, reduced Colorado River runoff, and longer fire seasons - all of which have become our current reality. 
  

Randy’s dedication and strategic insight enabled him to mobilize communities around climate action, particularly in our region. Through his collaborations with utilities and local governments, Randy championed renewable energy and energy efficiency, pushing the [City of Aspen](https://aspen.gov/518/Climate-Action) and [Holy Cross Energy](https://www.holycross.com/) to national recognition in green power leadership.
  

Randy also co-founded the Association for the Study of Peak Oil USA and spoke globally on energy’s complex challenges, inspiring action by helping audiences navigate the complexities of energy development. 
  

Beyond his professional work, Randy was an avid outdoorsman and champion of the natural world. He skied across Baffin Island and explored Colorado’s high country. 
  
Randy’s legacy lives on in CORE’s work, and his influence shapes today’s clean energy initiatives. Known for his large heart and wild mind, he inspired a generation to address our energy future with courage and imagination.  

  * ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Randy_Udall_Winds_WBoyles20110817_0012-1920w.jpg)

[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Coerdert+Case+Study+%281%29-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
###  [Rebuilding with Resilience: How One Colorado Couple Created an All-Electric, Solar-Powered Home After Devastating Fire](https://www.aspencore.org/rebuilding-with-resilience)
By Julie Kapala • January 29, 2026
When a catastrophic fire destroyed Clint Coerdt and Kate Sartain's home in Old Snowmass, Colorado, they faced an impossible choice: leave the Roaring Fork Valley or rebuild in the shadow of devastating loss. What emerged from the ashes is a blueprint for resilient, all-electric mountain living powered almost entirely by the sun--and it could inspire your own home energy transformation.
[ ![Image of the  The Diane and Bruce Halle Center for Hope and Healing in Basalt, Colorado](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/HalleCenter-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
###  [Building a Zero-Emissions Healing Center in Colorado](https://www.aspencore.org/building-a-zero-emissions-healing-center-in-colorado)
By Julie Kapala • November 9, 2025
Learn how a nonprofit overcame floodplain and zoning challenges to build a sustainable healing center that sets a new standard for green construction.
[ ![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Tara-1920w.jpg) ](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
###  [Energy-focused Basalt nonprofit announces new chief executive officer](https://www.aspencore.org/energy-focused-basalt-nonprofit-announces-new-chief-executive-officer)
By Aspen Times • September 22, 2025
The Community Office for Resource Efficiency has announced the appointment of Tara Stitzlein as the new chief executive officer. Stitzlein takes the helm from John Dougherty, who was appointed by the board as the organization’s contracted CEO in 2023. She is “marking a significant milestone in the organization’s history and the broader climate movement,” a press release states. “I am honored to continue serving CORE as CEO, building on the legacy that John and the previous climate leaders at CORE have shaped.” she said in the release. “The urgency of the climate crisis demands that we expand our impact while ensuring that our work remains community-rooted. I am thrilled to steward CORE’s mission and make climate action accessible for all residents throughout Pitkin, Eagle, and Garfield counties.” Dougherty will remain with CORE for a transitional period to support Stitzlein in her new role. Her official start date in this new role in Sept. 15. She holds a Master of Science in Biology, with a concentration in Molecular Environmental Biology from The Arctic University of Norway, where she researched the marine plastic microbiome for her thesis. She is currently pursuing a Master of Legal Studies in Environmental Law at the University of Denver. She has also served in various leadership roles at CORE since June 2022, most recently as the director of Climate Action Programs. She has overseen operations, strategy, personnel management, and significant projects like the Coal Basin Methane Capture initiative. ﻿ “We are thrilled to welcome Tara as our new CEO,” said Tessa Schreiner, CORE’s board chair, in the release. “Her extensive experience as a leader in climate action, coupled with her impressive educational background as a scientist, makes her the perfect fit for CORE at this pivotal time. Tara’s unique blend of scientific expertise and passionate commitment to environmental sustainability aligns seamlessly with our mission. We are confident CORE can scale climate solutions to meet the increasing urgency of the climate crisis, and we believe that under her leadership, CORE will expand its impact and further engage the community.” And Stitzlein is no stranger to the Roaring Fork Valley. Her husband, Cole Green-Smith, is a native of the area who graduated from Aspen High School and currently works as a hydrologist for the U.S. Forest Service, bringing over a decade of experience in public service. They reside in Missouri Heights with their 16-month-old daughter, June. “This personal connection to the community further enhances Tara’s commitment to leading CORE and making a positive impact in our region,” the press release states. Stitzlein will be at CORE’s Green Expo on Sept. 12 at the Limelight Hotel in Aspen. The community is encouraged to attend this event from 1-5 p.m., followed by a social hour from 5-6 p.m. where attendees can meet her and learn more about her vision for the future. The event is free and open to the public — registration can be completed at aspencore.org/green-expo . CORE has pledged to address climate change “swiftly, impactfully, and courageously while enhancing its capacity to combat the climate crisis.” CORE aims to align community priorities with climate action and bridge the gap between ambitious climate goals and measurable action. For more information about CORE and Stitzlein’s vision, visit the aspencore.org or contact the organization directly.

Sadie Kenyon-Dean

![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/Sadie-Kenyon-Dean-CORE-Staff-1920w.png)
### Sadie Kenyon-Dean
Office Manager
* * *
Originally from Upstate New York, Sadie’s commitment to sustainability and environmental justice took root during the We Are Seneca Lake campaign, when her local community organized to prevent the expansion of fracked gas storage. She carried that passion to Haverford College, earning a B.S. in Physics and conducting her thesis on light pollution and its environmental impacts.
  
Before joining CORE, Sadie tried on many different hats in Philadelphia, working as a high school teacher, jeweler, Excel tutor, and, most recently, as a payroll administrator. She is thrilled to have found a role where she can use her eclectic background and enthusiasm for organizational efficiency to help affect meaningful change in her local environment.
  
Outside of work, Sadie can be found running, hiking, skiing, crafting, reading, or spinning out unbelievably ill jams on her mixer.  

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
970.925.9775  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
sadie@aspencore.org

Sam Johnston
* * *
![](https://lirp.cdn-website.com/06c12080/dms3rep/multi/opt/CORE-Staff-Sam-Johnston-1920w.png)
### Sam Johnston
Energy Concierge, Residential Programs
* * *
Born and raised in Basalt, Sam developed a deep love for the natural environment and the Roaring Fork Valley from an early age. Growing up surrounded by mountains, rivers, and open spaces shaped her appreciation for the outdoors and inspired a strong commitment to caring for the place she calls home. In 2025, Sam graduated from the University of Colorado Boulder, with degrees in Environmental Studies and Sociology along with a couple certificates in Public Health. After briefly attending law school for environmental law, Sam realized community-based solutions and approaches to climate change better aligned with her values and career goals in the environmental space.
﻿
In her new role as an Energy Concierge, Sam works with residents to make home energy upgrades more accessible and approachable. She enjoys helping community members navigate electrification, energy efficiency improvements, and available resources, with the goal of reducing greenhouse gas emissions.
  

Sam is excited to be back working in the community where she grew up and is passionate about helping the Roaring Fork Valley build a more sustainable future. When she is not working you can find her skiing Snowmass, in the kitchen baking, or hiking the trails near Ruedi Reservoir where she lives.   

A black and white drawing of a telephone on a white background.
[970.239.7305](https://www.aspencore.org/)  

A black and white envelope icon on a white background.
sam@aspencore.org
